Review Rules 125

Article 1: All motions submitted for review should be reviewed separately by the following groups according to their nature:

(1) Compulsory Education Group (2) Adult Supplementary Education Group (3) Teacher Training Group (4) Elementary Education Group (5) Secondary Education Group (6) Higher Education Group (7) Social Education Group (8) Overseas Chinese Education Group (9) Mongolian and Tibetan Education Group (10) Education Funding Group. Article 2: Members of each review group shall be appointed by the Speaker from among the members and submitted to the general meeting for approval. When necessary, specialized members of the Education Program Compilation Committee and the head of the relevant department of the Ministry of Education may attend to provide explanations. Article 3: Members of each review group may also serve on another review group and may request the Speaker's approval to switch to another group. In addition to the members of the Education Funding Group, one person from each of the other nine groups should be selected to join the review. Article 4: Each group shall have one chairman and one secretary, elected by the members of the group. Article 5: The meeting time of each group, in addition to the meeting schedule, may be determined and notified by the chairman of each group, but shall not conflict with the general meeting time. Article 6: Each group may hold subcommittee meetings and joint meetings with related groups to facilitate the review of motions. Article 7: The discussion of motions in the review meeting shall be decided by a majority of the members present. If the members have two or more opinions on the same motion, the second most numerous opinion shall also be attached and forwarded to the general meeting. Article 8: The review meeting shall report the results of the review of each case to the general meeting and appoint one person to explain the outline. If it is deemed necessary to amend the original proposal, an amendment shall be drafted and submitted to the general meeting. Article 9: All motions passed or amended by the review meeting shall be collected and included in the general meeting agenda by one of the secretaries of the meeting. Article 10: These rules shall be implemented upon approval by the Second National Education Conference.

Detailed Rules of Procedure 126

Chapter 1: General Provisions Article 1: The seating arrangement for members of this conference shall be determined by lottery. Article 2: The President or Vice President of the conference shall serve as the chairman. Article 3: The meeting time shall be three hours per day. If the chairman deems it necessary, the time may be extended, but not by more than thirty minutes. Article 4: Motions and meeting agendas shall be printed and distributed to all members in advance.

Chapter 2: Meetings Article 5: This conference may only convene if more than half of the members have reported their attendance. Article 6: All speakers must first stand and report their number. Article 7: No two or more persons may speak at the same time. If two or more persons report their number at the same time, the chairman shall designate the order of speaking. Article 8: Members discussing motions shall not involve matters outside the scope of the motion. Article 9: Each member's speech shall not exceed five minutes. Article 10: Each person's speech on the same motion shall not exceed twice, except for answers or to draw attention. Article 11: If the chairman wishes to participate in the discussion, he may step down to his seat to speak and be replaced by the Vice President or the President as chairman. Article 12: The chairman may declare the end of the discussion during the meeting.

Chapter 3: Provisional Motions Article 13: If any member encounters a major issue, he may make a provisional motion, but it must be seconded by more than ten members present.

Chapter 4: Review Article 14: All motions shall be submitted for review first. Article 15: Review rules shall be determined separately. Article 16: Review committee members should report the review results of each case to the general assembly and appoint one committee member to attend and explain. If it is considered necessary to amend it, an amendment should be drafted and submitted to the general assembly.

Chapter 5: Voting Article 17: The motions of this conference shall be decided by a majority of the members present. If members have two or more opinions on the same motion, the second most numerous opinion may also be attached and forwarded for approval. Article 18: When voting, the chairman shall first read out the motion to be voted on and vote on them separately. After voting, members may no longer discuss the motion. Article 19: The voting methods are divided into raising hands and standing. However, if the chairman consults the members and there is no objection from the entire room, the case shall be passed without having to go through the procedures of raising hands or standing.

Chapter 6: Attendance and Leave Article 20: If a member is unable to attend due to illness or other reasons, he must state the reasons and ask the chairman for leave. Article 21: When a member attends, he shall sign his name in the attendance book. Article 22: After attending, a member may not leave the meeting unless it is adjourned or during a break, or with the permission of the chairman.

Chapter 7: Supplementary Provisions Article 23: These detailed rules shall be implemented upon approval by the Second National Education Conference. Article 24: If there are any matters not covered in these detailed rules, or places that need to be amended, they shall be amended by a resolution of this conference.

Conversation with Huang Shiheng, Director of the Hunan Education Department 127

Mr. Huang Shiheng, Director of the Hunan Provincial Department of Education, and Mr. Huang Dujie, representative of the county education bureau directors of the province, arrived in Beijing on the 12th. The reporter had the following conversation with Director Huang:

1. Education Funding:

(a) The provincial education funding for the 17th year of the Republic was more than 1.88 million yuan. In the 18th year, it increased to 2,630,532 yuan, an increase of more than 750,000 yuan. The percentages of each item in the total education funding are detailed below: (1) Elementary education funding accounts for 4%; (2) Secondary education funding accounts for 40%; (3) Higher education funding accounts for 13%; (4) Private school subsidies account for slightly more than 13%; (5) Social education funding accounts for 22%; (6) Overseas study funding accounts for 5%.

The provincial education administrative expenses are not included in the provincial education funding. Starting from the 18th year, the provincial government allocates 8,410 yuan per month, totaling approximately 100,928 yuan per year.

(b) Local education funding: The 69 counties in Hunan have a total of 5,484,450 yuan. Hunan Province has a total of 76 counties, and the reports from seven counties have not yet arrived, so they are not included. The estimated total amount of funding for each county should be more than 6,030,000 yuan. The highest is Changsha County with 420,000 yuan per year, Xiangtan with 380,000 yuan, and Xiangxiang with 300,000 yuan. The lowest is Tongdao County with only 6,000 yuan. The percentage of local education is as follows: A. Elementary education accounts for 71.70%; B. Secondary education accounts for 6.50%; C. Social education accounts for 3.48%; D. Education administrative expenses account for 13.89%; E. Others account for 5.04%.

2. Regarding the Situation of Primary School Education: Before the 16th year of the Republic, the majority of the education sector in Hunan Province was manipulated by the Communist Party. After the May 21 Incident, the authorities sought to eliminate the Communist Party and improve teacher quality, conducting examinations for primary school teachers. Since the 17th year, the affiliated primary schools of provincial schools have increased funding and improved the treatment of vocational education staff. Recently, efforts have been made to promote compulsory education, and a provincial compulsory education committee has been established in the province, and county compulsory education committees have been established in various counties to plan the implementation of compulsory education.

The survey of the number of schools in 60 counties, including Xiangtan, in the 17th year is as follows: (1) 11,967 junior primary schools; (2) 327 complete primary schools; (3) 282 senior primary schools; (4) 7 provincial affiliated primary schools (excluding kindergartens). The total number of schools is 12,583.

Expanding primary school funding is very difficult, and there are four reasons for this: (1) Previously, temple property could be allocated to education funding. Since the Ministry of Interior promulgated the Temple Custody Regulations, it has been impossible to allocate it. (2) The surtax on tobacco and alcohol was originally one of the sources of local education funding. Now, due to the Ministry of Finance's cancellation of this tax, the source has been greatly reduced. (3) Previously, each county could raise funds on its own. Now, the Ministry of Finance supervises local finances, and the Ministry of Finance representative Xu Shouzhi's restrictions are extremely strict, making it difficult to open up new sources of funding. (4) Among the old cases in various counties that have been approved and allocated to education funding, financial institutions often consider them to be exorbitant taxes and fees and cancel them. Judging from the above four points, increasing education funding requires the formulation of new regulations and increasing the people's productive capacity. According to precedents in various countries, the popularization of compulsory education requires the state to raise large sums of money for subsidies. This is a practice that can be adopted.

3. Vocational Education: The Provincial First Vocational School, the First Agricultural School, the First Industrial School, and the Provincial First Women's Vocational School are all located in Changsha. The Second Vocational School is located in Changde, the Third Vocational School is located in Hengzhou, the Fourth Vocational School is located in Shaoyang, the Sixth Vocational School is located in Zhijiang, and the Eighth Vocational School is located in Guiyang. The separate establishment of vocational schools in various counties is to promote the balanced development of education in various counties. There are 17 private vocational schools in Changsha, 12 of which receive subsidies from the province. There are 15 county-run vocational schools in various counties. There are a total of 44 vocational schools in the province. 4. Normal Education: The Provincial First, Second, Third, Fourth, Fifth, and Sixth Middle Schools all have senior high school normal departments. The Provincial First Agricultural School has an attached rural normal school, which started in the spring of the 18th year. The First Men's Normal School is located in Changsha, and the school building for the Provincial First Women's Normal School is under construction. The Faculty of Arts of Hunan University also has an education department, which is an institution for training teachers for secondary schools. There are 35 county-run normal schools in various counties throughout the province.

4. Secondary Education: The Provincial First to Sixth Middle Schools (three for boys and three for girls) are coeducational and have senior and junior levels. The First Middle School (boys) and the Second Middle School (girls) are located in Changsha, the Third Middle School (boys) is located in Changde, the Fourth Middle School (girls) is located in Taoyuan, and the Fifth Middle School (boys) and the Sixth Middle School (girls) are located in Hengzhou. There are seven middle schools jointly established by several counties. Since last year, they have all received subsidies from the province, which is also intended to promote the balanced development of education. There are 25 independently established county-run middle schools (without provincial subsidies). Compared to the two, the joint county middle schools are better run. There are 24 private middle schools that receive provincial subsidies and 15 that do not receive provincial subsidies. There are a total of 78 middle schools in the province.

5. Higher Education: Hunan University is a provincial university formed by the merger of high-level engineering, agriculture, and commerce colleges. It was established during the Zhao Hengti era and was once suspended and renamed Zhongshan University. It is now still named Hunan University and has three colleges of arts, science, and engineering, as well as a preparatory course. The monthly funding was more than 16,000 yuan in the 17th year and more than 18,000 yuan in the 18th year. There is also an additional temporary fee of 10,000 yuan per month. Although the school's expenses are small, it has produced many talents. Many serve outside the province, but not so many serve in the province. Efforts are now being made to expand facilities and enrich content. The library is under construction, and instruments and books are also being added. By the 19th year, the annual temporary fee can reach 200,000 yuan, and the regular expenses can also exceed 20,000 yuan. The future of Hunan University has promising prospects. In addition, there are three private universities that have not yet been registered with the Ministry of Education: Qunzhi Political Science and Law University, Jianguo Political Science and Law University, and Medical University.

6. Social Education: The province has established a provincial popular education committee, which publishes many popular education publications. There is a provincial popular education hall, a museum, and the Zhongshan Library. Each county also has a popular education committee, which is in charge of popular education matters throughout the county. Recently, the province has built a new public sports field and spent more than 100,000 yuan to build a Zhongshan Hall for public lectures. There are 31 popular education halls, 18 lecture halls, 86 libraries, 23 newspaper reading rooms, 346 people's schools, and 17 poor people's handicraft factories throughout the province.

7. Characteristics of Hunan Education: (A) Open funding: The province has been able to fully achieve this. To build a clean government, we should start with the education sector. Since the 17th year, there have been no delays in payments. Since the beginning of the Republic of China, the temporary fees issued in the 18th year of the Republic have been the most. The open method is that the provincial education department organizes an economic audit committee to review the accounts of the department and publishes them once a month. A funding management committee is established throughout the province, with seven or eight representatives publicly elected by the education sector throughout the province as members, responsible for auditing the expenditures and income of the provincial education funding, which is also published once a month. The interest of 7,000 to 8,000 yuan is entirely for public use. The accounting directors of provincial schools are directly appointed by the education department, and the principals can only supervise them. Each school also organizes an audit committee, which is also responsible for supervising the accounting director. The education department, the finance department, and the Hunan audit committee also audit them. Under this kind of joint supervision, the accounting director absolutely does not commit fraud. The continuous disputes in the education sector of other provinces, the lack of open funding, is the biggest reason. Hunan has overcome various difficulties to achieve the goal of having the department appoint accounting directors. (B) Balanced development of education throughout the province: Provincial schools can be distributed to remote counties, and the joint middle schools receive provincial subsidies, which is also one way to promote the balanced development of education throughout the province. The salaries of the education bureau directors of various counties are directly paid by the province on a monthly basis, not from county funds. For counties where the education funding is less than 15,000 yuan, the province subsidizes 60 yuan per month. The purpose is also to promote the balanced development of education in the province. (C) Establishment of libraries in various counties: In the first half of last year, there were very few libraries in the province. In the winter, the education department ordered each county to establish a public library within three months. All counties were able to comply. There are now 86 libraries throughout the province.

Conversation with Jiang Ji, Director of the Jiangxi Education Department 128

▲The State of Education in Jiangxi Province

Jiang Ji, Director of the Jiangxi Education Department, came to Beijing yesterday to attend the Second National Education Conference and stayed at the Central Hotel. The reporter visited him on the morning of the 15th and had a detailed conversation with him about the education situation in Jiangxi. The report of Jiang Ji is divided into the following items:

(A) Elementary Education (1) Public Junior Primary Schools: 1956 schools, Private: 5203 schools (233,950 male and female students); (2) Public Senior Primary Schools: 45 schools, Private: 54 schools (4999 male and female students); (3) Public Complete Primary Schools: 216 schools, Private: 345 schools (48,568 male and female students); (4) Other (Kindergarten students and supplementary schools equivalent to elementary school level): Public: 13 schools, Private: 3 schools (910 male and female students). In total, there are 7,835 primary schools with a total of 288,427 male and female students.

(B) Secondary Education (1) Junior Middle Schools and Junior High Departments of Complete Middle Schools: Provincial: 15 schools for boys (including 7 schools with junior high departments of complete middle schools), 4 schools for girls (including 1 school with junior high department of complete middle school), a total of 4,200 male and female students. Municipal/County: 9 schools for boys and 1 school for girls, with 1,212 male and female students. Private: 17 schools for boys with 2,324 students. In total, there are 46 junior high schools (35 schools established independently, 11 schools with junior high departments of complete middle schools) with 7,736 students. (2) Senior High Schools (i.e., Senior High Departments of Complete Middle Schools): Provincial: 8 schools for boys with 56 classes, 3 schools for girls with 12 classes, totaling 1,283 students (including 588 in general courses, 612 in normal courses, 20 in art courses, 12 in business courses, 26 in kindergarten normal courses, and 25 in arts courses). Private: 4 schools for boys with 949 students. In total, there are 15 schools with 2,232 students. (3) Normal Schools: Provincial: 1 rural normal school with 200 students (?), County: 3 schools with 271 students, Private: 1 school with 60 students. Note: (Senior high school normal courses have been mentioned earlier). In total, there are 5 normal schools with 471 students. (4) Vocational Schools: Provincial: 8 schools for boys and 1 school for girls, totaling 1,011 students. Public: 1 school for girls with 40 students. Private: 1 school for girls with 28 students. In total, there are 10 schools with 1,079 students.

(C) Higher Education (1) Provincial Vocational Schools: Law School: 6 classes in undergraduate program and 2 classes in preparatory program; Agricultural School: 4 classes in undergraduate program and 2 classes in senior high program; Medical School: 5 classes in undergraduate program; Engineering School: 5 classes in undergraduate program and 8 classes in senior high program. In total, there are 637 students. (2) Students Studying at National Universities Outside the Province: Approximately 270-280 students. Other students studying at private universities and vocational schools: According to surveys, there are already hundreds of students. (3) Government-Funded Overseas Students: 14 in Europe and America, 78 in Japan. Subsidized students: 13 in Europe and America, 16 in Japan. According to investigations, there are also hundreds of students who are purely self-funded without subsidies.

(D) Social Education (1) Social Education Institutions: The province originally had 9 institutions, and each county and city has a total of 96 institutions. (2) People's Supplementary Schools: The number of schools established by each county and city totals 803, with 26,278 students. The number of schools attached to provincial and private schools totals 44, with 1,592 students. The number of schools attached to social education institutions totals 6, with 256 students.

The Process of Drafting the Plan for Improving Social Education and Its Main Points - Chen Jianxiao 130

Generally speaking, this plan includes: (1) planning vocational supplementary education for agriculture, industry, and commerce; (2) preparing for the establishment of various major social education institutions (such as public theaters, public sports fields, public libraries, museums, and art galleries); (3) promoting special education and reformatory education; (4) improving customs and promoting public entertainment methods; (5) stipulating cooperative methods for social education and school education; and (6) an outline for implementing this plan. The original assumed program items varied greatly in detail. The original specified items were: (1) determining the implementation goals and methods of social education; (2) planning vocational supplementary education for agriculture, industry, and commerce (such as working with the Ministry of Agriculture and Mines to vigorously promote agricultural extension services); (3) promoting and encouraging art education and planning and establishing central and provincial music and art museums; (4) planning the establishment of central and provincial libraries and compiling various supplementary reading materials, popular readings, and general materials; (5) preparing for the establishment of central and provincial museums and formulating concrete measures for preserving documents and antiquities; (6) promoting public sports and implementing the Physical Education Law promulgated by the National Government; (7) planning special education for the mentally and physically challenged, and reformatory education for criminals; (8) planning for the improvement of customs and public entertainment matters (such as improving opera, storytelling, shadow puppetry, and establishing model theaters and public tea houses) and methods for supervising and guiding social education institutions established by public and private organizations; (9) drafting "National Independence Movement Education" methods from the perspective of social education; (10) stipulating matters related to social education and school education (such as setting up social education institutions attached to rural primary schools); (11) drafting types and procedures for civic education and public training. Its classification should be the same as originally planned, or even more detailed, because there were not many drafts provided by the invited drafting experts, and the level of detail varied. Later, it was revised several times casually, so it became very uncertain. This is what I feel very sorry about when describing the drafting process. This plan does not include: (1) civic education such as party ideology training; (2) public education such as public supplementary schools. These are also worth noting. However, public education has already been published in the Adult Supplementary Education Plan. Party ideology education and company education were initially assigned to the Party Ideology Education Group, although it was not expected that this group would not be established in the end.

In general, party ideology propaganda, political training, and the cultivation of citizens' exercise of four rights were originally placed within the scope of social education. Therefore, four years ago, Sun Yat-sen University in Guangzhou established a Political Training Committee. The first section of the Social Education Department within the Graduate School the year before last seemed to be the Social Education Section outside of schools, in charge of the Three Principles of the People education, etc. Now, higher-level schools still have Moral Education Committees. These all recognize social education as education for cultivating healthy citizens, completely eliminating the concept that social education is somewhat empty and impractical in the eyes of ordinary people. This has had a very good influence. However, since the discussion about education being entirely based on the Three Principles of the People, it seems that we should not fragmentedly talk about party ideology and politics. We must dissolve them into curriculum materials and moral education, to prevent people from studying party ideology like studying "Party Eight-legged Essays." Only then can we separate party ideology education, etc., from social education.

As for public education, it has been mixed up with social education from the beginning, so it is still difficult to explain them clearly. Although these two types of education are the same in nature, they differ in quality due to the size of their scope. They are absolutely not to be confused. Public education targets individual members of the public. In very popular terms, it uses a method to make the illiterate literate and to provide those without knowledge and skills with general knowledge and living skills. Social education, however, has different circumstances. It often pays attention to general social culture and academics, as well as public customs and habits. It targets not only individual members of the public but also the entire society. Naturally, its scope is very large. It can take into account all aspects of the public's moral, intellectual, aesthetic, and physical education. The main parts of public education are public schools and adult vocational supplementary schools. Therefore, public education is also a formal form of social education. However, this plan does not include public education because there is another adult supplementary education plan at the same time.

The above is the historical evolution of the expansion and contraction of the scope of social education. This plan is also based on this process.

Drafting this plan was similar to drafting other education plans. Initially, the Ministry of Education, based on the resolution of the Second Plenary Session of the Third Central Executive Committee, established the Education Program Drafting Committee, which set up a Social Education Group. It hired Gao Yang, Tang Maoru, Chen Yangzao, Liu Zhanen, Zhu Maocheng, Fu Ruoyu, and me, a total of seven people, as expert committee members. It also invited Chang Daozhi, Sun Shaobo, Zhu Chongtao, Yu Youren, Yun, and Gu Shaoyi to draft specific items. As drafts from various parties were sent in one after another, some were detailed, some were brief, and some were missing without any drafts. Because of my position in the Ministry of Education, I also served as the director of this group. I carefully organized and sorted them out, made them separately, and then the program committee added, deleted, and revised them before they were completed. Then, the Ministry of Education combined it with other plans for implementing or improving education, calling it the "National Education Improvement Program," and submitted it to the Executive Yuan for submission to the National Government, which sent it to the Central Political Conference for review. Only then could it be sent to the National Education Conference for discussion. The procedure of so many twists and turns and meetings and reviews cannot be said to be not meticulous and thorough. However, some places wasted precious time discussing trivial issues, and sometimes discarded many valuable or even necessary materials because they disliked the plan's content being too rich and the length being too long. It is true that there were unavoidable circumstances, but I still think it is a pity. For example, the item of planning special education for the mentally and physically challenged and reformatory education for criminals was later changed by the program drafting committee to planning methods for setting up special education and reformatory education, removing the mentally and physically challenged and adding delinquent children or youths. As for the methods of reforming criminals, it is now stipulated that the Ministry of Education should first set up a testing and research office to test the psychology of criminals, and then organize a research committee on reformatory education courses to determine curriculum standards. In each province, the education department should also cooperate with the provincial court to conduct trials in the provincial prisons, and then gradually promote it to various cities and counties. This is much simpler and less detailed than the initial plan. Initially, Mr. Zhu Chongtao saw in the newspaper that the Ministry of Education had organized an education program drafting committee divided into eleven groups, and that blind, deaf, and disabled education was uniquely missing, and he argued fiercely. He wrote an initial draft of a program for blind, deaf, and disabled education in China, arguing that blind, deaf, and disabled education should deserve special attention from educators, and listed it as a unit in the education program. He also argued that in terms of laws and regulations, attention should be paid to (1) determining the status of blind, deaf, and disabled education in educational administration; (2) Zhou Gengsheng, representative of Wuhan University on the left, and Huang Jianzhong, Director of the Hubei Education Department on the right; the goal of blind, deaf, and disabled education; (3) how the blind, deaf, and disabled school system should be formulated; (4) the curriculum issues of blind, deaf, and disabled schools; and in terms of implementation, pay attention to (1) the estimation of the number of blind, deaf, and disabled children nationwide; (2) the funding issues of blind, deaf, and disabled education; (3) the training of teachers; (4) the steps to promote blind, deaf, and disabled education. Also, Mr. Yu Youren's submitted program for blind, deaf, and disabled education also planned the goals of blind, deaf, and disabled education, teaching methods, moral education standards, and methods for promoting blind, deaf, and disabled education in great detail. Unfortunately, due to limited space, it was not included in this plan. Fortunately, these proposals mostly belong to practical implementation aspects, and in the future, it will not hurt to have the local design test and promote them.

In addition, there are also (1) methods for improving customs and promoting public entertainment and (2) drafting national independence movement education from the perspective of social education. The latter method was drafted according to the intention of the Central Training Department. From the standpoint of nationalism, using educational methods to teach the public and youth to understand the situation of our country being oppressed by foreign imperialists, to invigorate and strive for China's freedom and equality. Its method also starts from using lyrics and novels, etc., and has many similarities with the former method of improving customs and promoting public entertainment. The former method is relatively detailed, its purpose is to promote beautiful social customs, cultivate good public habits, reform old social bad habits, implement a happy and harmonious life for the people, and promote the noble and great spirit of the nation. Its methods for implementing the improvement of customs are divided into two types: passive and active. The passive one is to try to ban or prohibit the old bad habits and businesses that harm customs. The active one is to promote proper public entertainment. From the latter point of view, it can be said that to improve customs, it is necessary to promote proper public entertainment. On the other hand, if the public gets proper entertainment, customs will naturally be improved. The two are interrelated and cannot be separated. As for their implementation procedures, they are nothing more than several types of registration, training, review, punishment, or promotion and reward. However, these two methods were also not fully incorporated into this plan. Now, looking back on the process of drafting this plan, it is inevitable to feel that it is biased and incomplete, lacking in substance. When we draft and discuss plans, it is best to discuss the part that the plan itself can develop, and do not forcibly add a restriction from the outside. This restriction is not only useless for discussion, but also very easy to become an obstacle, hindering the advantages of the plan. Moreover, it is also unreasonable to regard social education as a side business, not as important as school education.

Now let me briefly mention a few points for discussion, so that it can be known where the simplicity, incompleteness, and regrets are. For example, the first part of this plan was to determine the goals and implementation methods of social education. Gao, Tang, Chang, and Sun provided materials and drafts. Its most brilliant point is that it is advocated that the goals of implementing social education should be determined according to our country's education purposes and its implementation guidelines. Our country's education purposes state that the education of the Republic of China is based on the Three Principles of the People, with the goal of enriching people's lives, supporting social survival, developing national livelihoods, and continuing national life, striving for national independence, universal civil rights, and the development of people's livelihood, to promote world harmony. The third item of its implementation guidelines states that social education must equip everyone with common sense of modern urban and rural life, skills to improve family economics, qualifications necessary for civil autonomy, habits of protecting public undertakings and forests and gardens, and the virtues of supporting the elderly, caring for the poor, preventing disasters, and helping each other. The seventh item states that schools at all levels and social education should pay equal attention to the development of national physical education. If the above-mentioned education purposes and their implementation guidelines are analyzed, they will become the following two tables:

Education Purposes

Supporting social survival and continuing national life: Social aspect

Developing national livelihoods and enriching people's lives: Individual aspect

World Harmony and National Independence: Social aspect

Universal Civil Rights and the Development of People's Livelihood: Individual aspect

Implementation Guidelines

Common sense of modern urban and rural life, skills to improve family life, development of national physical education, qualifications necessary for civil autonomy | Individual aspect

Habits of protecting public undertakings and forests and gardens

Looking at the above two tables, it can be seen that social education should take into account both the individual and society. From the individual's point of view, social education should enable each member of society to have continuous growth, regardless of gender, age, or level of education. In terms of knowledge, ability, spirit, and body, they should all have opportunities to continuously strive for improvement at any time. Therefore, national livelihoods can be developed and people's lives can be enriched. From the social aspect, social education should make each member of society a responsible, healthy, and productive citizen. Therefore, national life can be supported. Therefore, social education is divided into civic (i.e., national) education, livelihood education, art education, and health education. The educational goals of these items are listed in detail according to the above two tables, and a practical outline is first stated, from the outline to the details. The description and breakdown are very detailed, but later there was no chance to compile it into the plan.

Now, what remains of this plan and includes the important parts is another very simple summary of the plan. People who want to study the content of this plan or participate in this national conference and want to glimpse the full text but do not have the time can first look at that summary and use it as a stepping stone. Therefore, there is no need to say anything about key points or non-key points here. However, as far as this remaining plan is concerned, there are several implementation principles inside, such as (A) administrative organization should be simple, (B) various implementation agencies should be centralized, (C) implementation procedures should be tested first and then promoted, (D) implementation talents should be specially trained, (E) social education funds should be broadly raised and their independence should be guaranteed, (F) the government should guide society and use all its strength to promote social education. These are very important. The rest are mostly using these principles to solve various implementation problems. In addition, the classification of vocational supplementary schools, the annual preparation and promotion of public theaters, public education fields, public libraries, public museums and art galleries, and art exhibitions, as well as the cooperative and division of labor methods between social education and school education, are all the essence of this plan. In short, this plan has the above-mentioned process, making this plan seem to be pieced together bit by bit, and the spirit is not completely consistent and systematic from beginning to end. I hope that the education colleagues attending the meeting will not hesitate to add to and correct it.

Meeting Rules of Procedure 131

First, Section Chief Wu Yanyin read out the original text of the rules of procedure. Minister Jiang stated that these rules are based on the "Essentials of People's Rights". However, the reason why the opinion of the minority was attached to Article 17 was for reference when submitting it to the Central Government. Later, member No. 98 proposed a temporary motion of attending members, asking whether it could be changed to one-fifth or two-sixths. Xu Rongguang advocated for ten attending members. Zhu Jingnong said that if it is outside the scope of the program, the restrictions should be strict. Within the scope, ten people should not be determined. Zhao Naichuan said that the temporary motion of this proposal should be restricted to one-fourth of the attending members, not the number of registered members. Please pay attention to everyone. At this time, the chairman put it to a vote, saying that those who advocated maintaining the original proposal, please raise your hand. Forty-one votes were obtained. As a result, it was a minority. At the same time, Mr. Chen Bulei proposed that the endorsement of more than ten members present at the meeting should be a temporary motion, which received forty-nine votes and was passed by a majority.

For the draft of Article 10, Zhang Mojun advocated that the number of speeches per person for the same proposal should be changed to no more than three times, which received twenty-three votes and was not passed.

Discussion and Review Rules 132

Wu Yanyin still read out the review rules item by item first. Xiong Changfei proposed that Article 2 should be revised: "The members of each review committee shall be appointed by the chairman from among the members and submitted to the conference for approval." The following text should be deleted. Zhu Jingnong advocated that specialized committee members and responsible section chiefs should be allowed to attend and make statements, but not participate in the discussion. Zhang Mojun advocated that the review committee members should be determined by themselves, and the specialized committee members and responsible section chiefs should be allowed to attend the review. Zhu Jingnong advocated maintaining the method of the review committee members being appointed by the chairman. He agreed with the second half of Zhang Mojun and Yu Qingtang's proposal: "The members of each review committee shall be appointed by the chairman from among the members and reported to the conference for approval." The final decision was still maintained.

Educational Opinion Paper (3) - Gao Junshan 133

(5) The abilities of gifted children far exceed those of ordinary children. Ordinary teaching materials and methods are not only insufficient to make them work hard but also cannot arouse their interest. As a result, they will inevitably become disgusted with school life. However, if they are taught in separate classes, materials suitable for their abilities can be used. In this way, not only can their interest in learning be increased, but also the years of schooling can be shortened and the content of the curriculum can be enriched. Naturally, the results will be more considerable, and time and money will be more economical.

(6) Children with low intelligence can only deal with simpler and more concrete things. If the newly determined teaching materials can be adapted to the degree of their intelligence, then their academic performance will certainly be very good. They can use a skill to support themselves. This will reduce the burden on the family and increase social efficiency.

(7) Gifted children are the pioneers in future academics and the backbone of society. If no measures are taken to stimulate their abilities, they will inevitably spend their lives without any achievements due to the lack of opportunities for full development, or they will be contaminated by bad habits in the environment and fall. Now, if we can discover real gifted children and educate them, we will definitely be able to improve our country's position in the world of academics in the future, and with ideal leaders, we will definitely be able to realistically create happiness for the masses.

(2) Methods

(1) The Ministry of Education should hire education experts to jointly formulate special and detailed methods. After implementation, if shortcomings are found, they should be revised at any time.

(2) Schools at all levels should establish special classes for children with low intelligence or gifted children, depending on their talent equipment and economic capabilities.

(3) Refer to the achievements and methods of special education in Europe and the United States for reference.

(4) Each school should report the results and difficulties of the pilot program at any time for everyone's learning and research.

▲ Proposal to Stipulate Standards for Publicly Funded Students

(1) Reasons

(1) The history of our country sending students to study abroad has been very long. However, there has never been a fixed standard for the amount of public funds. Even when studying in the same country, there are differences in the amount. Because the standard is not fixed, there is nothing to follow. We have to listen to the free distribution of various agencies. In this way, the same publicly funded students also have phenomena of prosperity and decline.

(2) The units of public funds used in the past were also very inconsistent. Some used domestic silver coins as the unit (such as most provincial funds), and some used gold coins of the study abroad country as the unit (such as tuition fees of Tsinghua University). The price of gold fluctuates from time to time. Those using national currency as the unit have monthly tuition fees that increase or decrease accordingly.

(3) The amount of public funds is almost always based on past practices, without paying attention to the changes in the cost of living in the study abroad country. Therefore, the amount set ten years ago is still being used to this day, without knowing that the cost of living has increased a lot. Furthermore, in the past year or two, the price of gold has risen daily, which has invisibly reduced tuition fees in order to maintain the increased cost of living.

(2) Methods

(1) The Ministry of Education should hire people familiar with the situation of various countries to formulate a unified standard for public funds according to the current living conditions of each country so that the sending agencies have something to follow.

(2) At the same time, make a form and send it to the consulates and embassies of various countries, asking them to forward it to students studying abroad, people working and living abroad, and business people to investigate their cost of living. The materials collected can be used as a reference for setting standards.

(3) The unit of public funds should be the national currency of the study abroad country (such as francs in France and US dollars in the United States).

(4) Pay attention to changes in the cost of living. A new standard should be re-established every so often.

(5) Pay attention to the subjects studied. If necessary, issue some special funds to show fairness (such as the experimental fees for those studying natural sciences and the music fees for those studying music, etc.).

▲ Please the Ministry of Education to Limit the Dispatch of Students from Provinces and Institutions with Difficulties in Educational Funding to Study Abroad and How to Improve Later Cases

(1) Reasons

(1) Student tuition fees actually include tuition, food, clothing, housing, and pocket money. Once a problem occurs, not only can they not study, but they also find it difficult to maintain their lives. Students from slightly wealthy families can still be barely supported by their families. If the family is poor, they want to return to their country, but they have no money for the trip and have to sit and wait for death.

(2) People who cannot receive tuition fees on a monthly basis or often do not receive tuition fees for several months, assuming that their parents cannot support them and there is no other source of subsidy, most of them are in this situation. They have no choice but to look for work. People who cannot find work are hindered in their studies on the one hand and restricted by the study abroad country on the other hand. For example, the US government prohibits students from working. How painful and inconvenient!

(3) Hardworking students work on the one hand and still choose to study the prescribed courses on the other hand. As a result, their health will inevitably be damaged. This is not the meaning of the country cultivating talents.

(4) People with a weaker will will inevitably fall into a pessimistic situation.

(2) Methods

(1) The Ministry of Education should issue an order to all provinces and institutions that unless the educational funds are certain, do not send students to study abroad.

(2) After sending them, tuition fees must be pre-remitted on a monthly (or quarterly) basis, based on the date of receipt, and must not be overdue.

(3) Provinces or institutions with certain funds, if there is an unexpected problem, should try their best to maintain the public funds of the students who have been sent abroad.

▲ Teachers and Students of Universities, Middle Schools, and Primary Schools Should Wear Domestic Clothes and Use Domestic Materials

(1) Reasons

(1) At this time of expensive gold and silver, the loss of using foreign goods is even more alarming. Not wearing Western clothes is a very effective way to increase revenue and reduce expenditure. The materials for Western clothes are all wool fabrics, and most of the wool fabrics are imported from abroad. On the one hand, we suffer the loss of buying foreign goods with heavy money, and on the other hand, it is enough to hinder the development of domestic goods. Clothing is a daily necessity that cannot be lacking for a moment. Compared with the consumption of all educational supplies, such as stationery, instruments, and chemical medicines, the cost is much greater. Therefore, if people in the education sector can use domestic goods to make domestic clothes, it is a kind of relief for the country's finances.

(2) Every country has its own special fashion that cannot be forced to be the same. A country's clothing is the most prominent representative of a country and is also an expression of national characteristics. We should preserve the colors of our country and not imitate the fashion of other countries. Then we can promote the inherent spirit of the nation and arouse the concept of national unity. Unless it is a conquered country, its language, customs, etiquette, and clothing should not completely imitate the people of other countries.

(3) The cost of Western clothes is greater than that of Chinese clothes. Even the lowest materials are more expensive than Chinese clothes. Education is a poor profession, and the income of teachers and staff in middle and primary schools is particularly limited. If the price of Western clothes takes up a large part of their budget, is it not a very uneconomical thing? As for the students, it is giving their parents a heavier burden. It is not easy for middle-class families to send their sons to middle school or university. Adding the consumption of clothing is enough to hinder the opportunity of going to higher education. Isn't it penny wise, pound foolish?

Important News

National Scout Inspection News 134

▲Proclamation to the Public by the Headquarters

(1) To demonstrate the sound spirit of the nation.

(2) To promote the physical training of the people.

(3) To fully develop the five areas of intelligence.

(4) To deeply recognize the leadership of this Party.

The Headquarters of the Boy Scouts of China, in order to hold the first National Scout General Inspection, has issued a proclamation to the public. It first states that the holding of this Boy Scout General Inspection marks a new era in the history of Boy Scouts in our country. We deeply feel that this year is the most important and valuable period in the history of the development of Boy Scouts in China, as the sound spirit of the nation is demonstrated and the physical training of the people is promoted. We sincerely hope that all compatriots in the country will pay full attention. Next, it discusses the origin of the Boy Scouts, which was first founded by the Englishman Baden-Powell, and the evolution of Boy Scouts in China. Finally, it states that the Boy Scouts under the leadership of the Chinese Kuomintang bear the responsibility of realizing the Three Principles of the People, completing the Chinese National Revolution and building a new country of the people, by the people, and for the people. Today, most young people in China are decadent in their aspirations and weak in their bodies, truly exhibiting the spirit of the "sick man of the East," so the national spirit is almost exhausted. The Party's Boy Scouts must have a firm and clear national consciousness to maintain and promote the spirit and culture of their own nation, and must fully develop the five aspects of morality, intelligence, social skills, aesthetics, and physical education, in order to exercise civil rights and fulfill all other national obligations. Furthermore, they must have production and technical training, cultivate the habit of loving and using domestic goods, promote production, and support the development of people's livelihood. It also states that the purpose of this general inspection is to demonstrate the achievements of the training of each Boy Scout group, to encourage the good ones, and to find ways to improve the deficient ones. The Boy Scouts from various provinces and cities are gathered in the capital not only to connect the friendship between the Boy Scouts, but also to enable Boy Scouts from all places to have a deeper understanding of the significance of the Party's leadership. We also hope that all sectors of society will have a correct understanding of the Boy Scouts under the guidance of the Party, unite together, and promote the development of the Boy Scout cause in China.

▲The First Discussion Meeting

▲Chairman Zhang Zhongren Reports on the Order of Proceedings

At 2:30 PM on the 16th, the registration procedures for each group were completed, and the badges, group flags, etc. were also issued. Therefore, the Guidance Section of the Provisional Office convened the first discussion meeting for each group leader. Representatives from forty-seven groups attended. Chairman Zhang Zhongren reported as follows: (1) At 1:00 PM on the 17th, practice the inspection ceremony and action procedures at Xiaoying; (2) Xiaoying is now dry, and the camping problem can be decided by the 17th at the latest; (3) At 10:00 AM on the 17th, convene a meeting of all group leaders to explain the general inspection format and action procedures; (4) Due to weather conditions, all competitions will be suspended and as many performances as possible will be added; (5) It is planned to publish a special publication for this general inspection and grand camping. Please have each group write a short essay about the situation from departure to the present and submit it to the Drafting Section for publication. Furthermore, each group leader can write a brief history of the establishment of their group and submit it to the Drafting Section for整理刊登編輯專刋.

▲Chairman Chiang to Attend and Deliver a Speech

Chairman Chiang Kai-shek of the National Government notified the Boy Scout Inspection Office that he will personally attend the general inspection ceremony on the 18th and deliver a speech.

▲Rumor of Postponement of Commander-in-Chief's Inauguration

General Commander of the National Boy Scouts, He Yingqin, is currently presiding over military affairs in Hankou. It is feared that he will not be able to return to the capital for the inauguration ceremony as Commander-in-Chief on the 18th, so the inauguration ceremony will be postponed.

▲Dai Chuanxian to Serve as Chairman of the General Inspection

The Chairman of the National Boy Scout General Inspection and Grand Camping, currently the Minister of Training of the Central Government, Dai Chuanxian, has returned to the capital from Shanghai and will serve as the chairman.

▲Relocation of the Office

The Provisional Office of the National Boy Scout General Inspection and Grand Camping has relocated its office to the National Government Military Officer Research Class on the 16th, for the convenience of handling matters as the inspection and camping are imminent.

▲Enthusiastic Participation

The participation of Boy Scouts from all over the country in the National Boy Scout General Inspection and Grand Camping is extremely enthusiastic.

▲Competitions Changed to Performances

The Boy Scout Headquarters has decided that the competition program is too numerous and the time is not sufficient for allocation. Furthermore, various competitions are limited to a few participants and cannot be joined by all. In order to fully demonstrate the true spirit of the Chinese Boy Scouts, all competition programs are changed to various performances.

▲Issue of Food Rations

The Boy Scout Inspection Office has stipulated the standard for issuing food rations for Boy Scouts through the Food Service Section of the Affairs Department, as follows: 14 ounces of rice, 4 ounces of vegetables, 4 ounces of pork, 4 ounces of sweet potatoes per person per day, 1 bottle of soy sauce for every 10 to 15 people, 2 bottles for every 16 to 20 people (and so on). The above items are issued once a day. 2 ounces of bean oil and 8 mace of salt are issued all at once. Rice bags and soy sauce bottles must be returned after use. The issuing time is from 1:00 to 3:00 PM every day.

▲Office Stipulates Registration Date

▲2,000-3,000 People Have Registered

The Boy Scout General Inspection Office stipulates that all Boy Scout groups participating in the inspection must register uniformly on the 16th. Therefore, those who went to register before the 16th were extremely enthusiastic. From 8:00 AM to after 9:00 PM, those who registered still came in droves. It is estimated that two to three thousand male and female Boy Scouts and representatives from Shanghai, Beijing, Jinan, Jiangsu, Ningbo, Zhejiang, Hangzhou, Wujiang, Qingdao, Shaoxing, Jiaxing, Southern Jiangxi, Nanchang, Nantong, Anqing, Anhui, Changsha and other places have registered.

▲Negotiating to Change the Inspection Location

▲Ten Schools Designated by the Beijing Bureau of Education for Reserve Use

The Boy Scout General Inspection Office estimates that the number of participants will exceed 5,000, and the address of the Military Officer Research Class may not be able to accommodate everyone. In order to prevent阴雨起见, it is heard that the Ministry of Training has been consulted to inform the Beijing Municipal Bureau of Education to designate ten schools in the city for temporary use.

Chinese Boy Scout Commander Supplementary Oath Ceremony and First National General Inspection Ceremony Program

I. Chinese Boy Scout Commander Supplementary Oath Ceremony

(1) First order to prepare

(2) Second order to prepare (each group lines up in order)

(3) Third order to prepare (each group lines up to salute)

(4) Raising the national flag

(5) Chairman, Supervisor, and Commander take their positions

(6) Singing the Party song

(7) Bowing with the highest respect to the Party flag, the national flag, and the portrait of the late Premier

(8) The Chairman respectfully reads the late Premier's will

(9) Chairman's report

(10) Commander's oath

(11) Instructions from the Supervisor and Central Representatives

(12) Presenting the Commander's flag

(13) Speeches by guests

(14) Commander's reply

(15) Cheering by all

A. Long live the Chinese Boy Scouts

B. Long live the Chinese Kuomintang

C. Long live the Republic of China

D. Long live the Three Principles of the People

E. Long live, long live, long long live

Note:

When cheering, the master of ceremonies will wave the flag to lead

Everyone will shout out each sound left and right following the flag

The sound should go from low to high and from slow to fast

At the last word of the cheer, all Boy Scouts will raise their staffs high and throw their hats high.

(16) Ceremony concludes

II. First National General Inspection Ceremony of Chinese Boy Scouts

(1) Order to prepare (each group gathers in order, each squad lines up in order)

(2) Order to assemble (everyone forms a shape)

(3) Report on the total number of inspections

A. Squad leader reports to the group leader

B. Group leader reports to the sub-commander

C. Sub-commander reports to the commander-in-chief

D. Commander-in-chief reports to the commander

(4) Commander's inspection

A. Division

B. Rest

C. Basic movement exercises

D. Procession

(5) Commander's speech

(6) Dismissal

The Municipal Bureau of Education Obeys Orders to Investigate Shanghai University 139

▲If it still has a Department of Religious Studies, it should be ordered to stop.

Private schools must not make religious subjects compulsory, nor may they conduct religious propaganda on campus. The Ministry of Education has repeatedly ordered the educational authorities of various provinces and cities to轉飭遵照在案. It is now heard that the Municipal Bureau of Education has received instructions from the Ministry of Education to investigate Shanghai University, which still has a Department of Religious Studies and a Department of Theology, which is inconsistent with the law. It is ordered to conduct a detailed investigation. If the aforementioned departments still exist or if religious subjects are compulsory, they must be ordered to stop immediately, etc. After receiving the order, the Bureau will send personnel to investigate in order to submit to the Ministry for review. News of Our Country's Preparation for the Far Eastern Games 144

Our country is actively preparing for the 9th Far Eastern Games, sparing no effort. The other day, the National Sports Federation held a standing committee meeting and decided on all important plans. The details have been recorded in this newspaper. Here is the latest news:

(1) Applying for Public Leave

The selected representatives will organize a training institute and hire experts to serve as instructors. The instructors are currently being sought. The Sports Federation will apply for public leave on their behalf.

(2) Telegram to Overseas Athletes

Due to the lack of talent in the country, it is necessary to recruit athletes from overseas Chinese communities. For example, the Honolulu Chinese baseball team has sufficient strength and has agreed to return to the country to serve. The association sent a telegram to the Singapore Chinese Sports Organizations yesterday, inviting tennis star Lin Wangsu and the five best swimmers, whose travel expenses will be provided by the association. They will depart for Japan with all the athletes in the future.

(3) Arrangement of the Training Institute

The men's training institute has leased a three-story Western-style house at 190 Sabu Road, which is quite elegant. The rooms inside are all numbered, and there are also coaching rooms, management rooms, and hearing rooms. Each floor has a fixed number of servants to take care of everything.

(4) Purchasing a Large Number of Documents

Most of the selected representatives are students. From participating in each district's preliminary election meeting to the National Games, and then to Japan, it takes several months of time, which prevents them from studying and greatly hinders their academic work. In order to remedy this, the association has not only hired experts to give lectures, but has also purchased a large number of Chinese and Western documents and distributed them to both male and female departments to facilitate the athletes' research.

Mr. Chu Minyi's Letter of Thanks for Awards from the Jiangsu Provincial Games 147
