Yesterday's General Assembly of the Chinese Ratepayers' Association 148

Five Chinese Directors Elected, Six Chinese Committee Members, Twenty-Seven Executive Committee Members

The Public Concession Chinese Ratepayers' Association held its third general assembly at Gaozheng Hall at 4:00 PM yesterday. Wang Xiaolai and Chu Jiqing were publicly elected as Chairman and Vice-Chairman, respectively. With 59 representatives present, the quorum was met. The assembly elected Yuan Ludeng, Yu Qiaqing, Xu Xinliu, Bei Songsun, and Liu Hongsheng as the five Chinese directors to the Municipal Council, and Lin Kanghou, Qin Runqing, Chen Tingrui, Li Fuxun, Qian Longzhang, and Wu Yunzhai as the six Chinese committee members. In addition, twenty-seven executive committee members were elected. The meeting adjourned at 7:00 PM. The details are as follows:

▲ Meeting Agenda (1) Ringing the bell to commence the meeting; (2) Electing the chairman; (3) Paying three bows to the portrait of Dr. Sun Yat-sen and the national and party flags; (4) Reverently reading Dr. Sun Yat-sen's will; (5) Chairman's opening speech; (6) Report by the directors and committee members attending the Municipal Council; (7) Electing five directors and six committee members to the Municipal Council; (8) Electing twenty-seven executive committee members of the Association; (9) Discussing the amendment to the Association's charter (proposed by Representative Yan E'sheng); (10) Discussing the proposal that all official notices of the Municipal Council use Chinese as the primary language and English as the secondary language (proposed by Representative Wang Yansong); (11) Discussing temporary motions; (12) Ringing the bell to adjourn the meeting.

Chinese Director Yuan Ludeng

▲ Representatives Present A total of 81 representatives belong to the association. Yesterday, 59 representatives attended, as follows: Zhang Yichen, Shen Bokui, Yu Xiji, Chu Jiqing, Zhang Rulin, Chen Yizhou (represented by Xu Jiqing), Cao Rangzhi, Yan E'sheng, Hu Fengxiang, Li Fuxun (represented by Hu Fengxiang), Li Bohan, Shen Tianxin, Chu Huiseng, Jiang Yiping, Jiang Yinan, Qian Longzhang, Wang Jie'an, Wu Yaqin, Chu Yunan, Zhang Yichen, Shi Zhikun, Lin Kanghou, Hu Mengjia (represented by Lin Kanghou), Yuan Jinchu, Sun Jingxi, Bei Songsun, Pan Xulun, Tu Zhongxuan, Zou Quan, Chen Tianyin, Sun Tieping, Wu Cangmin, Xu Tingzuo, Chen Guangfu (represented by Bei Songsun), Zou Xieqing, He Shaogeng, Lu Fengzhu, Zhang Zilian, Pan Gongbi, Chen Wenya, Xie Zhongfu, Xu Busun, Zhang Henghai, Yang Guoshu, Xiang Rusong, Yu Qiaqing, Fang Jiaobo, Wang Xiaolai, Ye Fuxiao, Huang Chujiu, Wang Yansong, Qin Runqing, Shi Liangcai (represented by Wang Xiaolai), Cheng Xiechun, Yuan Ludeng, Zhu Yinjiang, Lu Wenshao, Gu Zhuxuan, Wen Lanting, Wu Yunzhai, Wu Zhihao, Lu Feibo Hong, Tu Kaizheng, Chen Tingrui, Geng Jiaji representing the Municipal Government, and Ye Mingji representing the Shanghai Office of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs.

▲ Chairman's Speech Chairman Wang Xiaolai said in his speech: "Representatives of the Shanghai Office of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, representatives of the Municipal Government, and fellow representatives of the Association, today is the first meeting of the third general assembly of the Association. It differs from the first meetings of the previous two general assemblies in two aspects. First, the previous two general assemblies were held several days earlier than the Western ratepayers' meetings. This time, it is held on the same day, which indicates that the administration of the Public Concession is now jointly managed by Chinese and foreign ratepayers. The only reason why there is no assembly hall in Shanghai large enough to accommodate all ratepayers, and even if there were such a hall, it would be difficult to achieve effective deliberation by bringing all Chinese and foreign ratepayers together due to language barriers, is that it is hard to have a broad discussion. Second, in the previous two elections, there were only three seats for directors to the Municipal Council. This time, it has increased to five seats. However, due to these two differences, the responsibility of this general assembly is felt to be heavier and greater than that of the previous assemblies after pioneering work. According to the organizational method of this general assembly, it has been implemented for three sessions. The original drafter was Representative Yan E'sheng, who is present today. His intention was to take the strengths of the general parliamentary organization and remove the weaknesses of not being able to concentrate the social elite. He combined the ideals of the political system of Representative Russell and occupational representation, which is a combination of vertical and horizontal societies. On this type of organization, the *Eastern Miscellany* magazine has had articles discussing it, taking the same meaning. Mr. Fessenden, consultant to the Municipal Council, praised the perfection of the Association's organization when he met with me and Representative Xu Jiqing. This shows that whether an organization is good or not needs to be tested. The fact that it is now praised is something that Representative Yan probably did not anticipate when he first drafted it. I was fortunate to be the chairman of the previous meeting. With the support and guidance of the Vice-Chairman Xu and the three standing committee members, Lu Feibo Hong, Wu Yunzhai, and Cheng Xiechun, as well as all the executive committee members and representatives, I am able to relinquish my responsibilities today. However, at this time of handover, it seems appropriate to briefly report on the situation of the Association over the past year. The important matters are scattered in a booklet of important documents of the Association that is now in front of everyone. (1) The most worthy of mentioning in the past year is the increase of two seats for directors to the Municipal Council. Although the number of director seats in the Municipal Council should be based on the proportion of taxes paid, the number of Chinese directors should be 11 out of 20. This is a huge concession made by our Chinese people, not based on population, and a desire for fairness. Currently, only two seats have been added, for a total of five seats, which is far from this desire for fairness. However, 'traveling far begins with the near, and ascending high begins with the low,' which has been the policy adopted since the establishment of the Association. Therefore, although this increase is not satisfactory, the precedent of gradual increase has already begun today. However, I must say one thing here, that is, the increase of these two seats was originally agreed upon orally by Representative Yu Qiaqing and Mr. Fessenden, the former Chairman of the Municipal Council, when mediating the two-percent extra tax in 1927. Unexpectedly, the previous directors, Bei Songsun, Yuan Ludeng, and Zhao Jinqing, based on the exchange of documents between the Association and the Municipal Council, and this oral agreement, proposed a motion to increase the number of Chinese directors by two. Chairman Fessenden did not put it to a vote, believing that the time was not ripe, and simply replied. The previous Association sent a letter to Xu Mo, the former Jiangsu Commissioner for Foreign Affairs, to continue the negotiation, and Director Yu Qiaqing, Director Yuan Ludeng, Director Xu Xinliu, and the committee members made various contacts and efforts. The former Chairman and directors of the Municipal Council also understood the intention that the number of Chinese directors must be increased, and finally a resolution was made to propose an increase. At the same time, the Association also received a notification from the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, approving the Minister's reply to the notification of the increase. This is something that the Association and all the Chinese people in the concession should thank the foreign affairs authorities, all the directors and committee members, and Mr. Arnold, the director-general of the Municipal Council. (2) The two-percent extra tax was paid under protest, and it has been more than two years. Regarding the origin and process of the two-percent extra tax, the facts revealed in the minds of our people still cause pain. Paying rights under protest is an irresistible act under the law, and a humiliating method for those who implement high pressure. In this year's budget of the Municipal Council, after negotiations between our directors and committee members and the foreign affairs authorities, it has been decided to abolish this two-percent extra tax on July 1 this year. However, the legal procedures for the refund or agreement of the Chinese taxpayers for the two-percent extra tax paid under protest for two years have not yet been completed. The Municipal Council is plotting ways to resolve it. (3) The May 30th Massacre caused national outrage and shocked the world. Sixty to seventy people were killed or injured, and the other losses are unknown. At the beginning of this year, the compensation aspect has been resolved through the efforts of the directors of the May 30th Cemetery, Yu Qiaqing, Yuan Ludeng, and Cheng Xiechun. A total of 150,000 silver dollars has been agreed upon, which is double the original amount. However, the compensation for losses is still pending, and it is hoped that the foreign affairs authorities and the new directors and committee members attending the Municipal Council in this session will complete their work. (4) The Association has not relaxed its efforts to abolish consular jurisdiction. It has twice telegraphed the foreign affairs authorities, requesting them to take decisive measures to abolish it by decree. And for various incidents that requested the government, such as those that could not be implemented due to consular jurisdiction, the consular jurisdiction was severely attacked. The current government has already announced at the end of last year that consular jurisdiction would be abolished from January 1 this year. In addition, in cases such as the rejection of Japanese Ambassador to China Oobata Yuukichi and the case of British soldiers beating Zhang Xueliang to death, the Association either followed other groups or took the lead, proceeding based on the opinions of all the Chinese people in the concession. This should be clear to all representatives. Now, please representatives elect five directors and six committee members to the Municipal Council. After the ballots are counted, elect twenty-seven executive committee members of the Association, and then discuss various important proposals. My speech is lacking in style, please forgive me."

▲ Report by Chinese Directors Director Yuan Ludeng, representing the Chinese directors and committee members attending the previous Municipal Council, reported: "Today is the first meeting of the third general assembly of the Chinese Ratepayers' Association of the Shanghai Concession. All the honorable representatives are leaders of the citizens and respected figures in society. We, as the directors and committee members who participated in the municipal administration of the Public Concession in the second session, should report to the representatives on the major affairs we have participated in over the past year. We hope for your consideration. (1) Distribution of committees. Regarding the organization of the Public Concession Municipal Council and the conduct of its administration, the first session of directors and committee members reported to the previous general assembly, so I will not repeat it here. There are a total of 12 committees in the Municipal Council this session. The distribution of committee members and the number of people are as follows: 1. Police Committee: A total of 5 members, with Chinese occupying 2 seats, held by Director Yu Qiaqing and Committee Member Chen Tingrui. 2. Public Works Committee: A total of 4 members, with Chinese occupying 1 seat, held by Director Yuan Ludeng. 3. Finance Committee: A total of 6 members, with Chinese occupying 2 seats, held by Director Xu Xinliu and Committee Member Qin Runqing. 4. Health Committee: A total of 7 members, with Chinese occupying 2 seats, held by Director Xu Xinliu and Committee Member Qian Longzhang. 5. Staff Committee: A total of 4 members, with Chinese occupying 1 seat, held by Committee Member Li Fuxun. 6. Public Utilities Committee: A total of 6 members, with Chinese occupying 2 seats, held by Committee Members Bei Songsun and Lin Kanghou. 7. Music Committee: 2 members, all foreigners. 8. Transportation Committee: A total of 4 members, with Chinese occupying 1 seat, held by Committee Member Chen Tingrui. 9. Foreign Education Committee: 5 members, all foreigners. 10. Chinese Education Committee: A total of 6 members, with Chinese occupying 3 seats, held by Director Yuan Ludeng and Committee Member Lin Kanghou. In addition, there is Mr. Nie Yuntai, who was separately appointed by the Municipal Council. 11. Library Committee: 4 members, all foreigners. 12. Public Sports Field Committee: 4 members, all foreigners. (2) Establishment of Director-General. After Mr. Johnson retired from the Municipal Council, the position of Commissioner-General held by him was abolished. Last year, the position of Director-General was established, held by Mr. Fessenden, the former Chairman of the Municipal Council, to implement all resolutions of the board of directors. His powers are greater than those of the former Commissioner-General. (3) Increase in the Number of Chinese Directors. Increasing the number of Chinese director seats according to the proportion of taxes paid is a fair demand of all Chinese. When the two-percent extra tax issue was resolved the year before last, the mediator Yu Qiaqing discussed with the former Chairman of the Municipal Council, Mr. Fessenden, about increasing the number of Chinese directors by two last year. The previous directors, Bei Songsun, Yuan Ludeng, and Zhao Jinqing, also proposed to the Municipal Council, based on this agreement and the exchange of documents between the Association and the Municipal Council regarding the increase in the number of Chinese directors. The detailed process was recorded in the important documents of the Association last year, so I will not repeat it here. The colleagues in this session continued to work on it, and with the efforts of Mr. Xu Mo, the former Special Envoy of the Jiangsu Provincial Government for Foreign Affairs, and the understanding of the reasonable wishes of the Chinese people by the Chairman of the Municipal Council, Mr. Arnold, and the foreign directors, the entire Municipal Council unanimously resolved to propose a motion at the Western ratepayers' annual meeting this session to increase the number of Chinese directors by two, for a total of five. After this, there should be a total of fourteen Chinese and foreign directors in the Municipal Council. (4) Abolition of the Two-Percent Extra Tax. From July 1, 1927, the Municipal Council increased all municipal taxes (commonly known as patrol tax) in the concession from 14% to 16%, and municipal taxes outside the concession (i.e., in the extra-settlement road area) from 12% to 14%. At that time, Chinese taxpayers believed that the tax increase had not been agreed upon, and they protested. The Association seriously negotiated with the Municipal Council, and the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce and the Shanghai Road Merchants' Joint Association also took a consistent stance and jointly resisted. More than 40 stores were forced to close. Later, Yu Qiaqing took the position of mediator, and the two-percent tax increase was finally paid under protest under the name of a two-percent extra tax. Now the Municipal Council has resolved to abolish the two-percent extra tax, and the land tax has also been reduced from 8/1000 to 7/1000, which will be implemented from July 1 this year, and it has also been revised in this year's budget. This is the result of the united legal struggle of the former Jiangsu Commissioner for Foreign Affairs and all Chinese taxpayers. (5) Increase in the Salaries of Chinese Employees. Most of the senior staff of the Municipal Council are foreigners, needless to say. Even the middle-level staff are mostly foreigners, while the lower-level staff are mostly Chinese. There are many differences in the treatment of Chinese and foreign employees. The previous directors, Bei Songsun and Committee Member Li Fuxun, had negotiated with the Municipal Council, and the Council's senior staff should add more Chinese people. In addition to continuing to strive for the application of Chinese staff for senior positions, the colleagues of this session also advocated improving the treatment of all Chinese employees of the Municipal Council, with the principle of equality between Chinese and foreign employees. The Municipal Council has specially set up a salary committee to revise the salary and treatment regulations for Chinese and foreign employees. There are six members of the committee, and Chinese occupy one seat, held by Director Xu Xinliu. Since the meeting, the plan has been roughly formulated. In addition to the salary level, the principle is that Chinese and foreign employees should be treated equally. Before the salary level is decided, a temporary salary increase plan is implemented. All Chinese employees in the bureau will temporarily increase their salaries by 6% to 16% from January 1 this year. Those with higher original salaries will have a lower salary increase rate, which is 6%, and increase in turn until those with lower original salaries, the salary increase is 16%. (6) Construction of Primary School Buildings. The Municipal Council has never attached importance to the education of Chinese children, which cannot be denied. The previous directors and committee members proposed to expand Chinese primary school education based on the exchange of documents between the Association and the Municipal Council. The Municipal Council should first set up primary schools for three years to gradually increase them, and set up a Chinese Education Department to take charge of Chinese education administration, and hire educator Chen Heqin as the director. The Northeastern District Primary School has been open for nearly two years and has achieved good results. However, the Western District Primary School has not yet been opened due to the difficulty in finding a school building. At the beginning of our term, we believed that renting private houses to open schools was only an expedient measure. Therefore, we immediately proposed that the Municipal Council should raise huge sums of money to purchase land and build school buildings for long-term use. Now the Municipal Council has purchased ten acres and one point of land on Xinzha Road for the site of the Western District Primary School, and allocated about ten acres of surplus land from Nie Zhongcheng Public School for the site of the Eastern District Primary School. The construction cost of these two school buildings is estimated to be about 400,000 taels of silver. The Engineering Department of the Municipal Council is now drafting detailed drawings and will start construction soon, and it is expected to be completed within the year. As for the Northern District Primary School, it is currently borrowing private houses. The Municipal Council has decided to move into the Chinese Public School on Ai'erjin Road in the autumn. The Chinese Public School already has a larger school building, which is the original site of the former Thomas Hanbury Western Public School. In addition, education matters are detailed in another report. (7) Reorganization of the Provisional Court. The reorganization of the Provisional Court was implemented on April 1. When Chinese and foreign authorities negotiated the reorganization, we believed that this was the recovery of our country's judicial rights, which involved foreign affairs, and the Municipal Council should not interfere. The colleagues in the bureau and the Western taxpayers can understand this, and there are no obstacles. There are many other facilities, but they are all routine and there is nothing to mention. In short, we have not dared to slack off in the fight for the rights of the Chinese people in our duties. However, we are burdened with heavy responsibilities and often worry about failure. We are ashamed that we cannot live up to the trust of all citizens. Fortunately, the representatives have understanding. April 16, 1930, Reporters: Xu Xinliu, Yuan Ludeng, Yu Qiaqing, Qian Longzhang, Lin Kanghou, Chen Tingrui, Qin Runqing, Li Fuxun, Bei Songsun."

▲ Another Report Yuan Ludeng also reported on the general situation of Chinese education run by the Shanghai Public Concession Municipal Council: "The Municipal Council's original Huatong Public School, Yucai Public School, Nie Zhongcheng Public School, and Gezhi Public School had a total of more than 1,690 students in 1929, with annual expenses of 171,360 taels. Since the Chinese directors and committee members participated in municipal administration, the Municipal Council has added two primary schools in the Eastern and Northern Districts, which have been established for nearly two years. Now I will describe the situation of the two primary schools separately: (1) Students. The two primary schools in the Northeastern District began enrolling students on October 1, 1928. At that time, because schools everywhere had already started, and few people outside knew that the Municipal Council was opening new schools, the enrollment results were that the Eastern District Primary School only had 87 students, and the Northern District Primary School only had 78 students. In the spring of 1929, the number of students in both schools suddenly increased. The Eastern District Primary School increased from 87 to 413, and the Northern District Primary School increased from 78 to 396. Those who applied were still coming one after another. Due to the limited capacity of the school buildings, the two schools had to politely decline later applicants. In the spring of 1930, the Eastern District Primary School had 419 students, and the Northern District Primary School had 287 students, which was a slight increase compared to the previous semester. (2) Teachers. At the beginning of the opening of the two primary schools in the Northeastern District, each school only had 8 teachers, 1 principal, and 1 clerk, for a total of 10 teaching staff members per school. In the spring of 1930, the number of students suddenly increased. Due to the opening of more classes, the number of teachers in both schools increased from 8 to 16, for a total of 19 teaching staff members per school. In the spring of 1930, although the number of students was limited by the school buildings, there was no significant increase, but the number of classes gradually increased and the school affairs became more complicated. Each of the two schools increased one clerk, for a total of 20 teaching staff members per school. (3) Expenses. The regulations for the expenses of the two schools are that at the beginning of each year, the Chinese Education Department submits the budget to the Chinese Education Committee of the Municipal Council for review, and then it is implemented after being approved by the Board of Directors. (4) Matters that should be noted in the future. There are about the following points: 1. The area of the Public Concession is vast, and there are many residents. There are about 150,000 Chinese children of school age. Now the two primary schools in the Northeastern District have a total of 688 students, and the four Huatong Public Schools have a total of 1,690 students. Then, there are still 147,300 Chinese school-age children in the concession who do not have the opportunity to enter schools run by the Municipal Council. 2. According to the 1929 report of the Municipal Council, the Chinese education expenses in the Public Concession, in terms of the two primary schools in the Northeastern District, only account for 0.18% of the Municipal Council's annual revenue. Even if the expenses of the four Huatong Public Schools are included, it is still less than 2% of the total. Therefore, it is necessary to actively expand Chinese education in the concession."

Chinese Director Xu Xinliu

Page 14

▲ Three Proposals Executive Committee Member Wang Yansong proposed: "Respectfully, I would like to point out that municipal facilities must be based on facilitating the majority of citizens. Chinese people account for 80% of the citizens residing in the Public Concession, and the amount of taxes paid, even based on the figures announced by the Municipal Council, is 55% for the Chinese. Moreover, the actual number is more than this. However, all documents and announcements published by the Municipal Council are in English, making it impossible for the Chinese citizens who reside and pay taxes in the absolute majority to understand. This is inappropriate and this error should be corrected immediately. Please propose a resolution by the general assembly of this session, notifying the Municipal Council that from now on, all documents of the Municipal Council should be in Chinese as the main language and English as the secondary language, so that the majority of Chinese citizens can understand the current status of municipal facilities at any time, without further expectation." Executive Committee Member Yan E'sheng proposed: "To propose matters, I hereby submit a draft amendment to the charter in accordance with the provisions of Article 15 of the Association's charter. The main points are: (A) Changing the method of generating representatives. The original number of representatives was 81, generated in three groups, namely 27 people mutually elected by members, 27 people mutually elected by representatives of commercial organizations, and 27 people mutually elected by representatives of fellow-townsman organizations. However, based on handling experience, the number of fellow-townsman organizations is not large, and at the same time, the number of votes for mutually elected citizen members has increased every year. It is now proposed to amend it to: (1) 27 people mutually elected and re-elected by the previous general assembly; (2) 27 people jointly elected by representatives of commercial and fellow-townsman organizations; (3) 27 people mutually elected by individual members, still totaling 81 people. (B) Determining the method of generating representatives attending the Municipal Council. All Chinese directors and committee members attending the Municipal Council are generated by the general assembly. However, there is no clear provision in the charter. A provision should be added to show seriousness, and the quorum for this election meeting should be specified. I hereby submit one copy each of the original charter and the draft amendment to the general assembly for discussion." The above two proposals of the Shanghai Concession Ratepayers' Association were resolved to be handed over to the Executive Committee to form a review committee for review, approved by the Executive Committee, and then a general assembly will be convened for voting.

Chinese Director Liu Hongsheng

Annual Meeting of Western Ratepayers in the Shanghai International Settlement 149

▲ Motion to Increase Chinese Directors Defeated

▲ Motion Regarding News Reporters Amended

The annual meeting of Western ratepayers in the Shanghai International Settlement was held yesterday afternoon at 2:00 PM in the Municipal Hall on Nanjing Road. When the bell rang twice, not many Western ratepayers had arrived. Chairman Brigadier General Macnaghten stated that the meeting time had passed and proposed the first motion to elect Mr. Bael as chairman, seconded by Mr. Hibbard. The motion was unanimously approved by the attendees. After the chairman took his seat and read the notice of the meeting, he invited General Macnaghten to present the second motion to appoint Mr. Faillefeu as the meeting's recorder, again seconded by Mr. Hibbard, and unanimously approved by the attendees. General Macnaghten then proposed the third motion concerning the meeting's agenda, also seconded by Mr. Hibbard, and passed by the attendees. Then followed the fourth motion to approve the report and financial plan for 1929.

▲ Summary of Accounts: General Macnaghten then spoke, stating that the financial report for 1929 had already been distributed, and attendees were likely aware of its main points. The attached report from the Accounting Department summarized all important financial matters of the year, with detailed comparisons of actual and budgeted expenditures. Attendees could see that the Municipal Council strived to economize in all departments, staying within the budget. The ordinary budget for the year had a surplus of 3,534,830 taels, while the estimate was 500,896 taels. This was largely due to the Municipal Council's sale of the Electricity Department and the establishment of a sound method for paying the purchase price in installments with interest, which benefited the Municipal Council's finances. The summary of special income and expenditures for 1929 showed a surplus of 1,538,530 taels. The 4,400,000 taels in bond issuance approved at last year's annual meeting were not raised due to the sale of the Electricity Department. Furthermore, the Council did not intend to request permission from ratepayers to issue bonds in the coming years. The funds received in installments from the sale of the Electricity Department were deposited under the capital account, and all special expansion items were drawn from this account. Previously, due to financial difficulties, the road widening program had not been implemented, but now it was proceeding gradually. Although we are now in a position to handle all major expenses, we still carefully consider the urgency of any expenditure, avoiding any extravagance.

▲ Police Administration: The police administration was greatly reorganized with the assistance of Major General Joulard of the Indian Police. The number of administrative officials was reduced to the minimum, and three executive sections were established: Criminal, Special, and Reserve, each headed by a supervisor directly responsible to the Chief Constable. Four police districts were also established, each with an experienced District Superintendent assisted by a District Detective Officer to manage criminal investigations. Investigating crime was the main function of the police, and special attention was paid to this aspect during the reorganization. In the future, the records of criminal cases and the progress of police investigations should be more accurate than before. The number of detectives in each police station was previously too small, which was inconvenient, and it was important to increase the number. The service conditions of the Chinese police have been improved, and we are now planning to provide them with accommodation so that they can concentrate on their service, strictly observe discipline, and be willing to put forth their efforts in emergencies. Many high positions in the police administration are now planned to be filled by training well-qualified Chinese. The service conditions of European, Japanese, and Indian personnel have also been improved as necessary. The strength of the police force has been increased to keep pace with the development of the Settlement. In the past three years, various aspects of the Settlement have developed rapidly, causing the activities of various departments of the Municipal Council to expand greatly. Not only the police force, but also all departments have been able to cope with the increased responsibilities. This is something we can take comfort in.

▲ Salary Commission: After the Preparatory Committee submitted its report, the Municipal Council followed its recommendation and appointed a Salary Commission in May of last year to investigate the salaries of Chinese and foreign personnel in the Council. In order to abolish the existing allowance system in whole or in part, the Commission recommended paying actual salaries based on rank. The Municipal Council was unable to implement this measure immediately, and lower-level employees, due to the rising cost of living, were suffering and urgently needed temporary assistance. Therefore, the Commission was asked to pay immediate attention to this. During the Commission's discussions, opinions diverged, but after detailed deliberations in June, a temporary relief measure was devised, benefiting all low-paid married foreigners and all Chinese. This measure, after approval, was implemented by the Municipal Council. The Commission then proceeded to investigate employees and compile necessary information. Therefore, a regular meeting was held in November of last year, and the work is nearing completion, with the final report to be submitted soon.

▲ Municipal Economy: At last year's annual meeting of ratepayers, the Chairman of the Municipal Council, when speaking, mentioned the report of the Economy Committee, stating that he had been entrusted by the new Board of Directors to declare that the various recommendations of the Economy Committee would be diligently followed. One of the recommendations was that the committee or other similar groups continue their work indefinitely, assisted by two or more salaried specialists to manage everything. The Municipal Council, in order to maintain its affairs, had large expenditures, hence the establishment of the Economy Committee. Considering the committee's deep understanding of the overall situation, implementing this recommendation would require a large expense, which was not initially anticipated. The intention of the Municipal Council was to have an independent investigation conducted by someone who had been working with Chinese and foreign personnel for a long time and was familiar with their service conditions. The number of people with this qualification in this city was naturally limited, and Mr. Creagh was the most suitable. Therefore, he was hired to work with the Salary Commission, which was established at the time, to undertake this important task.

▲ Educational Improvements: The education of Chinese and foreign children in the Settlement has become increasingly difficult in recent years for various reasons, and is now one of the problems that must be addressed first. To facilitate Mr. Creagh's thorough reorganization of the Municipal Council's schools, he has been temporarily appointed as the acting director of the Education Department. The Western Boys' and Girls' Schools will be merged and located in the new building built on the site of the old Victoria Nursing Home, which will save money, improve equipment, and be more effective. The Chinese Public School on Elgin Road will now be moved to the Western School on Hanbury Road, which will increase the number of students by 250. After this proposal is implemented, the school buildings of the Municipal Council will all be Western-style buildings, and two large buildings will be vacated for other public uses. A Western primary school is now needed in the Western District to replace the current temporary school, but the site is difficult to find, and the Municipal Council's construction process is costly, so it has to be approached slowly. The Municipal Council has always taken an equal policy regarding the convenience of Chinese and foreign students in the Settlement to attend school. To promote this policy, it is planned to establish a Chinese primary school on the land recently purchased in the Western District. The current Northern District Primary School will be moved to the old Chinese Public School in that district. The Eastern District Chinese Primary School will be built on a portion of the land of the Nie Zhongcheng Public School to replace it. After this plan is fully implemented, it is expected that the annual cost of Western education will decrease compared to the present, while the annual cost of Chinese education will increase significantly. Now, taking this opportunity, I have a word to tell you, the burden of education costs may soon no longer be fully supported by taxes. The Municipal Council may discuss whether a certain percentage of the annual income can be used to fund education, or whether it will use part of it to subsidize educational institutions that have reached a certain level, regardless of their nationality. The Municipal Council, following the recommendation of the Economy Committee, hired a person familiar with the needs of Chinese and foreign schools to serve as the supervisor of the Education Department, assisting in the management of the Municipal Council's schools, and supplementing it with a permanent Education Committee composed of Chinese and foreign educators. The establishment of this committee aims to express the collective opinions of experts, assist the Municipal Council in handling all educational problems and needs, and seek to promote close cooperation between Chinese and foreign residents on the Municipal Council's educational affairs, which can achieve great and beneficial results.

▲ Provisional Court and Shanghai Special District Court: The agreement on the Chinese court in the International Settlement was signed in Nanjing on February 17, 1930, and immediately announced. After the full text was published, newspapers offered criticisms in opposition, causing the public to feel uneasy about the current political situation. When the Provisional Court Agreement was implemented on January 1, 1927, there was also widespread anxiety, saying that it would be greatly detrimental to foreigners. However, the adverse results found over time were not as serious as expected. I remember that at the annual meeting of ratepayers in April of last year, the Chairman of the Municipal Council criticized the actions of the Provisional Court. However, to be fair, the work of the Provisional Court has greatly improved in the past year. Judging from its current state, it is by no means as bad as the public initially believed. The general impression now is that cases of murder and robbery in the Settlement are emerging one after another, primarily due to the leniency of court judgments and secondly due to the laxity of general administration. Now, let me quote a section of the Municipal Council's annual report on police affairs to inform the public who are concerned about the facts, and the truth will be fully revealed. In 1929, the Municipal Council's police department prosecuted a total of 116,643 cases in the Provisional Court, of which 22,699 were serious criminal cases, with 20,441 convicted and 2,258 acquitted. This shows that in the cases prosecuted by the Municipal Council's police department in the Provisional Court, the defendants convicted accounted for as much as 90%. Compared with the courts of other major cities in the world, the result is commendable. Moreover, the judges of the Provisional Court and today's District Court are able to sincerely serve the public when they are free from interference from administrative officials. The frequent disagreements between the Municipal Council and the Jiang Court are often not due to improper investigations or unfair judgments, but rather because the concepts of judicial principles are fundamentally different between the Chinese and foreigners. In countries that implement new-era judicial systems, their courts are mostly independent and not mixed with government administrative organs, so they cannot be used as tools for implementing government administration. Under this system, individuals and their property are protected, and government officials cannot apply arbitrary, arbitrary, and illegal actions. Although the Nanjing government has recently established new-style courts based on the concepts of the new era of justice, it is a pity that it cannot place the Provisional Court or the court replacing it in a position free from interference from government administrative officials. As a result, the Municipal Council, which controls the police power in the Settlement, and the court frequently disagree, hindering it from being used by Chinese government officials as a tool to interfere in the municipal administration of the Settlement. China's insistence on not allowing its courts to break away from the interference of administrative officials is one of the most powerful arguments against the treaty powers abandoning consular jurisdiction before the time is ripe. According to the current articles of the Provisional Court Agreement, the representative of the consul has no real power, only the ability to protest. Therefore, it is difficult for the representatives to prevent the court from exercising the functions of administrative officials. Now, when the court exercises the functions of administrative officials to interfere with the rights of the Municipal Council, only the police department, acting under the direct orders of the Municipal Council, can deal with it, which is not, as generally believed, done by the consular representative. The representative appointed to negotiate the Provisional Court Agreement with China once consulted with the Chairman and Director-General of the Municipal Council. At the beginning of the discussion, it was informed that it was impossible to keep the consular representative in the same position as stipulated in the old agreement in the new agreement. The representatives of various countries also asked the Municipal Council to provide concrete suggestions on how to resolve the Chinese opposition to the layer of consular representatives. The Chairman and Director-General of the Municipal Council felt that the entire issue of police power and the Provisional Court and the new court was of great importance, especially the court's repeated attempts to exercise the functions of administrative officials. Therefore, they did their best to assist in the formation of a new agreement, gathering all the necessary powers that could be obtained in the hands of the police department. Now, the daily actions of the court are reported to the Municipal Council by the police department, which is the key to the overall situation. Therefore, the Chairman and Director-General of the Municipal Council had suggested to the representatives regarding the new agreement that they should do their best to prevent the new court from secretly trying cases in the new agreement. The Special District Court has now been established on April 1. It has not been long, and incidents have already occurred, indicating that the relationship between the Municipal Council and this type of new court in the future may be no less difficult than the old Provisional Court.

▲ Telephone: The telephone service in the Settlement has long been unsatisfactory to users. In June of last year, various chambers of commerce, organizations, and individuals jointly requested the Municipal Council to order the Delta Telephone Company to implement Article 3 of the 1925 Concession Agreement and begin improvements. The Municipal Council immediately began discussions with representatives of the company. The company representatives admitted that the poor condition of the telephone was due to: (1) the company's failure to anticipate the development of the International Settlement and the French Concession as they are today in the past few years; (2) the company's inability to raise the necessary funds for expansion; (3) the difficulty in purchasing materials during the years of the European War, resulting in mixed purchases; (4) the Municipal Council's rejection of the company's request to increase user fees two years ago; and (5) the discovery of so-called poor outdoor equipment conditions after the conversion to automatic telephones. The company, for financial reasons, was unable to remedy the situation. To make matters more difficult, before the company discussed the matter with the Municipal Council, it had accepted offers of financial assistance related to the manufacture of automatic telephone equipment and facilitating telephone services without submitting them to the Municipal Council for consideration, and had already made certain decisions. After lengthy discussions between the Municipal Council and the company, it was decided to hire an impartial expert for the Municipal Council's consultation and to notify the French Municipal Council of this move, which agreed. The company did not oppose the hiring of an expert, but felt that it would cause unnecessary delays, as the company had already made arrangements for improvements, and had installed automatic machines, and new machines ordered would arrive one after another. Waiting for the expert to arrive would stop the established procedures. Later, Mr. Anson submitted a report, and public opinion felt that it would be beneficial to the public to sell the telephone business to a financially strong organization that operated telephones. Now, there are three groups of representatives stationed in Shanghai, willing to bid to purchase the Delta Telephone Company. The three groups are competing fiercely for this matter. It concerns the public. If the actions of the two municipal councils or the Delta Telephone Company are seen as discriminatory in any way, it will cause a backlash. Therefore, the Delta Telephone Company decided to ask the three groups to bid to purchase it according to the current concession, and the director-generals of the two municipal councils and the company's representatives, Baker and others, would form an advisory committee to consider the bids together. Although the three groups have already submitted bids, the advisory committee believes that none of them can be accepted. Therefore, the two municipal councils decided to slightly amend the current concession as the basis for continued bidding or continued negotiations on the bids received. The municipal councils have disagreed on this amendment, so it has taken a long time to discuss and reach an agreement. On April 4, the concession amendment was sent to the company, which forwarded it to the advisory committee, which reopened negotiations with all parties concerned based on this method. It is currently in progress. After General Macnaghten finished his speech, he asked the audience to vote on the fourth motion, which was unanimously passed by the attendees.

▲ Fifth Motion: The chairman explained the fifth motion, saying that the 1930 budget had already been sent to the attendees for consideration and did not need to be elaborated on. It was found that under the regular section, the income and expenditure offset showed a surplus of 3,277,490 taels. However, if the police tax rate was not reduced from 16% to 14% and the land tax rate from 8/1000ths to 7/1000ths from July 1, restoring the old rates before 1927, the surplus would be much greater. I remember that at the annual meeting of ratepayers last year, the Chairman said that after the sale of the Electricity Department, the new Board of Directors would consider the issue of tax cuts. I am very happy to be able to fulfill my previous words today. As for the expenditure side, the police department's expenses increased by 43% compared to last year, which is 1,637,530 taels. This is a natural result of the large increase in the number of police officers in each police station, especially the number of Chinese police officers. The details are recorded in the Municipal Council's Gazette. Major Joulard's reorganization plan for the police force has been implemented under his command. This year, it is planned to add another team,

The Engineering Department also increased its expenses by 770,000 taels, mostly due to the difficulty of handling garbage and the increase in the cost of municipal property. It is planned to revalue the land prices as soon as possible, and the results should be seen in next year's budget. The fifth motion is proposed, "Please approve the 1930 budget and accompanying recommendations made by the old Board of Directors, so that the Bureau can collect various taxes in accordance with the budget." The audience passed it without objection.

▲ Sixth Motion: The Chairman began to explain the sixth motion, saying that the proposal to add three Chinese directors to the Municipal Council was passed by the Western Ratepayers' Annual Meeting in 1926 and subsequently approved by the diplomatic corps. However, after two years, Chinese in the Settlement began to nominate directors to join the Municipal Council. During these two years, Chinese representatives and Municipal Council representatives negotiated several times, trying to persuade the Municipal Council to make a firm agreement on the time and number of seats for future increases in Chinese directors. The Municipal Council did not want to be bound by this, and formally stated its position in a letter to the Chinese Ratepayers' Association on March 26, 1928, stating that the Municipal Council fully recognized that, according to the proposed method (three seats), if Chinese cooperation was complete, it would lead to an increase in the number of Chinese directors in the ordinary course of events, etc. Later, when the Chinese directors took office, there was indeed an understanding between Chinese and foreign citizens that the gradual increase rate of the number of Chinese directors in the future would be determined at least to some extent by the degree of cooperation of the Chinese directors. At the 1929 Western Ratepayers' Annual Meeting, the Chairman mentioned this matter, saying that the Chinese directors were all talented, far-sighted, and capable, and able to sincerely resolve the various difficult and complex issues of divergent views between Chinese and foreign people in order to enhance coordination and goodwill between the two sides, etc. As for the past year, the Chinese directors have also been able to cooperate fully to the extent possible in this mixed Chinese and foreign community, where the interests and views of various countries are sometimes difficult to compromise. I feel that in order to express sincerity and trust, we should take the initiative to find ways to increase the number of Chinese directors. Moreover, if this matter can be done automatically and quickly, it will greatly enhance Chinese-foreign friendship compared to reluctantly agreeing after bargaining. The Municipal Council's proposal to increase Chinese directors was announced before Judge Feetham came to Shanghai as a consultant. Judge Feetham's views on these issues cannot be announced until the report is prepared. However, he allowed me to declare that he believes that the passage of the motion to increase Chinese directors by this meeting would be beneficial to the public. Now, I respectfully propose the sixth motion, "Authorize the Municipal Council to request the countries concerned to increase the number of Chinese directors from three to five." A Westerner, Macdonald, then came forward to vehemently oppose it, saying that this kind of change would arouse ambition and be very dangerous. Although some guarantees have been given for the increase of Chinese directors, the person who gave this guarantee on that day was dancing with power, so this kind of guarantee is not enough to bind the ratepayers, etc. When the final vote was taken, this motion failed to pass.

▲ Seventh Motion: The seventh motion was then proposed, electing Mr. Brockman as this year's Land Reduction Committee member.

▲ Eighth Motion: The eighth motion was then proposed, electing four annual managers for the Public济 Hospital.

▲ Ninth Motion: Finally, the ninth motion was proposed, "News reporters should be allowed to attend and observe Municipal Council meetings as representatives of the public. However, when a majority of the council's directors decide, for the benefit of the public, that news reporters should leave the meeting, the news reporters should leave immediately. Also, the minutes of board meetings and committee meetings, after being approved by the Board of Directors, should be delivered to newspapers as soon as possible after each board meeting, except for those that should not be published for the benefit of taxpayers." The original proposer, Mr. Harris, stood up to explain, saying that the purpose of this motion was only to create an open public opinion and assist from the sidelines, in view of the fact that there are often extremely complex and important issues awaiting decision by the Municipal Council Board of Directors. The wording of the motion is very careful, hoping that everything important to us foreigners can be made public, while at the same time, there is a huge guarantee against leakage for those that should not be made public. The intention of this motion is not to give all newspaper representatives the right to attend. I mean that if this motion is passed, the Municipal Council will ask each newspaper to nominate two or three experienced and reliable representatives to enjoy the right to attend and observe exclusively, and distribute their news to various newspapers for publication. Therefore, it can be guaranteed that these representatives will be trained and qualified personnel. All directors can freely express their opinions, and there is no fear of inverting black and white and confusing the audience. Moreover, since the second section of the motion stipulates that the entire record of the meeting should be published as soon as possible, it can also provide a correction to the news recorded by the news reporters. Some say that since a detailed record has already been published as soon as possible, why is there still a need to attend and observe? I do not know that this record of the meeting must be published at the fastest 48 hours after the close of the meeting. In the eyes of the newspaper industry, it has become yesterday's news and is not enough to be called news. Moreover, the records of the meeting are all dull and tasteless, while the news published by newspapers must be fresh and sharp. I have discussed this matter with the editors and reporters of various newspapers, and they all said that if this motion does not have the first paragraph of the provision for attendance and observation, then the second paragraph of the provision for publicizing the record of the meeting will be of no benefit. Currently, Shanghai is the only major city in the world that does not allow newspaper representatives to attend municipal meetings. In the Hong Kong Legislative Council, even when there are issues that cannot be discussed publicly, news reporters are still allowed to attend, only not allowed to record and leak them. Only in this way can news reporters deeply understand the inside story of the motion, so that after the resolution is published in the future, it will be prevented from being an incorrect commentary. Fortunately, most of the newly elected directors agree to municipal openness. If we try to practice secret diplomacy again in the future, the result will inevitably be losses. I feel that the opinions of foreigners in Shanghai will not be ignored by the diplomatic personnel stationed in China, and at least they will be disregarded by their own government. The reason is that their own government often blames that the Shanghai Municipal Council meetings are kept secret, and the foreigners and taxpayers do not have a society that allows their opinions to be heard by the government, so how can the government know the thoughts and desires of you foreigners in Shanghai? Therefore, I hope that after news reporters are allowed to attend and observe Board of Directors meetings, a Western Taxpayers' Association will be organized at the same time, and an international committee will be elected to do its best to assist the Municipal Council and cooperate with each other, and when necessary, convene a meeting of taxpayers to present their opinions to the diplomatic officials stationed in China and to their own government, etc. Next, after the seconder, Mr. Marsden, made a brief speech, the Chairman of the Municipal Council immediately stood up and proposed an amendment, deleting the first paragraph of the original motion and retaining the second paragraph, and adding an explanation, saying that the proposal to allow the public to attend and observe Municipal Council Board of Directors meetings has now been proposed to the annual meeting of taxpayers for the fourth time. All three previous times were rejected by a majority, and this time the Board of Directors also invited the new directors of this session to discuss it in detail together. As a result, although it advocated as much publicity as possible, it was believed that news reporters should not attend and observe. The reason for this is, to take today's meeting as an example, if newspaper representatives are allowed to attend, in order to discuss freely, it will inevitably be necessary to ask news reporters to leave the meeting from time to time, which is not only cumbersome but also ridiculous, one. From a political point of view, Shanghai is going through an extremely serious period, and it is likely that diplomatic personnel will often submit to the Board of Directors for discussion the situation of negotiations on complex issues involving national sentiments. At this time, in theory, it seems possible to exclude news reporters, but in practice it is difficult to do so, two. There is a great danger of restricting the freedom of speech of the directors, making it impossible for them to express their opinions freely and frankly, three. After the Chinese directors joined, they can often freely and frankly express their opinions, which is of great benefit to solving difficult problems and enhancing Chinese-foreign goodwill. If there are news reporters present, it is believed that Board of Directors meetings will no longer be able to express their opinions as freely and frankly as before, four. Therefore, I propose the ninth amendment, "The entire record of Board of Directors meetings and committee meetings, after being approved by the Board of Directors, should be delivered to newspapers as soon as possible after each meeting, except for those that should not be published for the benefit of taxpayers." Later, the seconder, Mr. Davis, and Mr. Hughes spoke one after another, saying that there are six newspapers in Shanghai from China, Britain, America, Japan, France, and Russia. If news reporters are sent to attend and observe, they must all be allowed to attend without discrimination. When the final vote was taken, the amendment was passed by a majority, and the meeting adjourned at 4:40 PM.

▲ News After the Meeting: When the taxpayers' annual meeting was in progress, an Indian, claiming to be a communist, tried to break into the meeting place through the side door of the Municipal Hall. A Russian policeman greeted and stopped him. The Indian immediately punched him and fought with other policemen. Finally, he was defeated due to his inability to fight against many, and was captured by the policemen. Only after his hands and feet were tied could he be escorted to the Old Zha police station. During the mutual fighting, a Western police head was injured by the Indian.

Dramatic Change in the Shanghai Municipal Council's Chinese Councillor Issue 150

▲ Chinese Taxpayers' Association Elects Five Chinese Councillors

▲ Foreign Taxpayers' Association Rejects Increase Proposal

▲ Danger of Japanese Manipulation of Municipal Affairs

The Chinese Taxpayers' Association General Assembly and the Foreign Taxpayers' Annual Meeting of the Public Concession were held separately yesterday afternoon. The Chinese Taxpayers' Association, based on the Shanghai Municipal Council's January 6 resolution to increase the number of Chinese councillors from three to five, elected five Chinese councillors, Yuan Lvdeng, Yu Qiaqing, Xu Xinliu, Bei Songsun, and Liu Hongsheng, at a meeting yesterday to attend this term of the Shanghai Municipal Council. The Foreign Taxpayers' Association also held its annual meeting yesterday at City Hall. The Shanghai Municipal Council proposed the increase of Chinese councillors according to the regulations, but the result was a rejection. The Shanghai Municipal Council's Chinese councillor issue has therefore undergone a dramatic change. The assumption of office by the Chinese and foreign councillors of the Shanghai Municipal Council was originally scheduled for this afternoon, but with this sudden twist, not only is it impossible for the Chinese and foreign councillors to assume office today, but before a satisfactory resolution of this issue, it is feared that the Chinese and foreign councillors will be unable to meet. Yesterday, our reporter inquired about the attitudes of the newly elected Chinese councillors on this matter. All stated that they could not express any opinion until they received formal notification from the Shanghai Municipal Council. How to deal with this matter in the future will depend on the Shanghai Municipal Council's approach. However, according to private sources, the most difficult aspect of this issue is that in the Shanghai Municipal Council's proposal to increase the number of Chinese councillors, our side initially insisted that the ratio of foreign councillors to Chinese councillors should be nine to eleven. In August of the 17th year of the Republic (1928), Yu Qiaqing verbally agreed with the Shanghai Municipal Council's Feixin Dun that in the 18th year of the Republic (1929), Chinese councillors Bei Songsun, Yuan Lvdeng, and Zhao Jinqing wrote to the then Director-General Feixin Dun, requesting that he propose an increase. However, Feixin Dun neither submitted it to the board of directors for discussion nor submitted it to the taxpayers' meeting for resolution, but simply replied with his personal opinion. Subsequently, the Jiangsu Diplomatic Commissioner's Office, based on the final compromise proposal of the three Chinese councillors, negotiated with the leading consuls, hoping that the number of Chinese councillors would be increased by at least two this year. The leading consul then conveyed this to the Shanghai Municipal Council's Director-General for consideration. The Shanghai Municipal Council held a meeting on January 6 of this year and unanimously agreed to the resolution, which was communicated by the leading consul to the Diplomatic Commissioner's Office and forwarded to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs for reference. Therefore, the Chinese councillor issue has temporarily come to an end. However, this was still a compromise on our part. Who knew that the Foreign Taxpayers' Annual Meeting would reject the proposal yesterday? The Shanghai Municipal Council is now in a difficult position. They consider the taxpayers' annual meeting to be the highest decision-making body, but the Shanghai Municipal Council's resolutions have always been successfully passed in the annual meeting. The rejection of this proposal is tantamount to the annual meeting's lack of confidence in the Shanghai Municipal Council. The election of the five Chinese councillors is based on the exchange of official documents between the negotiating authorities of both sides, and they will not allow the established case to be overturned and make concessions again. Moreover, the Chinese side is not satisfied with the number of five Chinese councillors, and further negotiations will be necessary to increase the number. Therefore, if there is now a desire to return to the original number of seats, the Chinese councillors and Chinese committee members will take a unified attitude, refuse to attend meetings, and wait for the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to file a protest or promote the recovery of the concession. Furthermore, according to a certain legal scholar, this issue is a political issue, not a legal issue. The attendance of Chinese councillors on the Shanghai Municipal Council is an inherent right of the Chinese citizens of the concession. Now, the power to increase or decrease the number of Chinese councillors must be determined by the Foreign Taxpayers' Association. This means that the inherent rights of the majority of Chinese citizens are controlled by a small number of foreigners, which is fundamentally wrong. According to another source, the rejection of the proposal to increase the number of Chinese councillors at this Foreign Taxpayers' Annual Meeting was actually manipulated by the Japanese. The annual meeting has a total of about 1,200 voting rights, with the Japanese and British/Americans each holding half. When the proposal was put to a vote this time, about 200 British/Americans gave up their voting rights. Therefore, the Japanese, due to their failure to increase the number of Japanese councillors, used 600 votes against 400 votes to reject the Shanghai Municipal Council's proposed increase in Chinese councillors. It is said that the recent defeat of Arnold, the former Director-General of the Shanghai Municipal Council, in the election of foreign councillors was also manipulated by the Japanese. The Japanese will have a significant and dangerous influence on the future of municipal affairs in the concession.

Record of the British Chamber of Commerce's Annual Meeting the Day Before Yesterday 151

▲ Marshall's Speech on Commerce in China

▲ Brenan's Speech on Issues Regarding China

According to the "Zi Lin Daily", the British Chamber of Commerce in Shanghai held its 15th annual meeting at the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce yesterday (the 15th) afternoon. Chairman Marshall, British Consul-General Brenan, and Jameson, acting commercial secretary of the British Embassy, also attended the meeting. The chairman's speech summarized the current political, financial, and commercial situation in China, as well as the chamber's activities over the past year. He believed that the decline in silver prices was greatly influenced by instability in the interior and commercial depression. Therefore, the chamber advocated that instead of artificially raising silver prices, efforts should be made to eliminate obstacles to commerce in various provinces, encourage industry and commerce, and promote local prosperity. This would not only absorb the silver stored in Shanghai but also make the country unified and increasingly consolidated. He also stated that in the future, doing business in China would increasingly require proficiency in Chinese, which would soon become an indispensable language for merchants seeking success. He hoped that various foreign firms would send more junior staff to the meeting to learn. Last year, the number of unemployed British people in Shanghai increased significantly, with a total of 245 people registered. However, two-thirds of them have now found employment, etc. After the chairman's speech, the chamber's annual report and accounts were approved, and eight new directors, including Marshall, were elected. Then, the chairman invited the British Consul-General to speak. Brenan rose and addressed the audience, saying that they were all here for business, and that Britain's interests in China were mainly commercial. At a time when the country (referring to Britain) was facing financial pressure and high unemployment, maintaining and increasing export trade, preserving old overseas markets, and opening up new markets were fundamental priorities. If this goal could be achieved, even if it meant slightly harming the comfort and convenience of British residents, as well as purely local interests, it would be done. This was the British government's attitude towards all issues in China. However, to trade with others, it was necessary to maintain reasonable friendship. The national rights movement was one of the world's movements today, and all countries in the East were involved, including China. Any changes to the status of foreigners in China that were desired by the majority of educated and politically concerned Chinese people could not be ignored simply because they caused inconvenience to foreigners or were considered premature. The use of force would ultimately lead to mutual destruction, etc. After the British Chamber of Commerce's meeting ended, the China Association's annual meeting was held immediately, which also approved the association's report and accounts and elected new directors before adjourning.

The Rice Price Stabilization Committee Established Yesterday 152

▲ 10,000 Bags to Be Ordered Today

▲ Raising Funds to Cover Losses

▲ Plan to Raise at Least 100,000 Yuan

Rice prices in the city have been soaring, threatening the people's food supply. The Bureau of Social Affairs submitted a request to the mayor for approval to organize a Rice Price Stabilization Committee to purchase foreign rice to provide relief. All members of the committee have been appointed and commissioned by Mayor Zhang, and Director Pan of the Bureau of Social Affairs has been designated as the chairman of the committee. The committee held its first meeting, convened by Chairman Pan, at the Bureau of Social Affairs yesterday afternoon at 2:00 PM. The meeting was attended by committee members Wang Yiting, Mo Zijing, Huang Hanzhi, Ye Huijun, Yan Xiaoquan, Gu Xinyi, Yuan Liang, Tang Naikang, Chu Fu, and representatives Xu, Sun Yishan, Zhu Zixiang, and Lin Kanghou. Chairman Pan presided over the meeting, presented the rules of procedure for the meeting, which were discussed and passed, and decided to divide the work into groups to facilitate progress. Zhu Zixiang, Yan Xiaoquan, Gu Xinyi, and Sun Yishan were appointed as members of the Procurement Group, Lu Wenshao and Fan Hesheng as members of the Distribution Group, and Lin Kanghou, Ye Huijun, Wang Yiting, Huang Hanzhi, Xu Fu, Pan Gongzhan, Yuan Liang, Yao Zirang, Mo Zijing, and Weng Yinchu as members of the Finance Group, and they began work immediately. It is reported that negotiations will be held today to order 10,000 bags of rice from overseas, and more will be purchased at any time. Discussions were also held on how to cover the losses, and it was determined that the total amount to be raised from the municipal government and various organizations would be 100,000 to 150,000 yuan. The committee has sent letters to various parties to raise the full amount in the shortest possible time.

Central Government Orders Resolution of Pharmaceutical Industry Dispute 153

The Training Department of the Central Executive Committee sent a letter yesterday to the Shanghai Municipal Executive Committee, stating that the pharmaceutical industry labor dispute in Shanghai Special Municipality has been repeatedly reported by your committee and the Shanghai Special Municipal Government, as well as by the Shanghai Pharmaceutical Trade Association and the Pharmaceutical Workers' Union, all stating that this dispute has been mediated by your committee and others, but due to the extreme positions taken by both labor and management, it has not been formally resolved, and requesting that the matter be investigated and handled. The department dispatched personnel to investigate, and it was reported that both labor and management urgently needed a resolution. The department, based on the report and referring to the mediation methods proposed by your committee and the Shanghai Special Municipal Government, has formulated a method for resolving the pharmaceutical industry dispute in Shanghai, which has been submitted to the Central Government for approval. In addition to sending separate letters, we are enclosing the resolution method and sending it to your committee, together with the Shanghai Special Municipal Government, to instruct the Pharmaceutical Trade Association and the Pharmaceutical Workers' Union to comply with it. The progress of the handling must be reported in detail. The enclosed resolution method for the Shanghai pharmaceutical industry dispute is as follows: (1) There are currently more than 300 pharmacies in Shanghai Special Municipality, many of which are prosperous and have considerable profits. However, due to the large number of employers, there seems to be a shortage of manpower. Prosperous pharmacies can employ a larger number of workers. The Shanghai Labor Dispute Mediation Committee has approved more than 64 qualified workers. (2) Workers who are not qualified by the Mediation Committee should be compensated by the employer for their dismissal as a sign of consideration. (3) The pharmaceutical workers' strike this time is understandable, so the employer should pay half of the wages during the strike period as a sign of consideration. (4) The system of apprenticeships, replacements, and temporary workers in pharmacies should be handed over to the Shanghai Special Municipal Government for proper discussion and resolution after the labor unrest is resolved to eliminate disputes. (5) In the future, both labor and management must earnestly abide by the central government's laws and regulations, work together with one heart and one mind to seek the development of the pharmaceutical industry, and there must be no more disputes. (6) This method should be handled jointly by the Shanghai Special Municipal Party Department and the Municipal Government.

Major Fire in Nanshi This Morning 154

▲ Heavy Losses

At 2:45 AM this morning (the 17th), a fire suddenly broke out at the Hongqiao end in the city, and the red light filled the sky, making it impossible to approach. The streets and alleys around Hongqiao are extremely narrow, and the houses are densely packed and very old, making them prone to fire, so the fire spread very quickly. The fire brigades from various districts in Nanshi heard the alarm and drove their pumps to the scene to put out the fire. However, due to the narrow roads, it was difficult to deploy and shoot water. As of 3:30 AM this morning, when our newspaper went to press, the fire had not yet been extinguished. It is not yet known whether anyone was burned to death, but it is expected that the losses will be very heavy, truly a great disaster.
